<data key="y">0.4</data>
<data key="label">Military Planners, in Nod to Obama, Are Preparing for a Faster Iraq Withdrawal</data>
<data key="date">2009-01-15</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  Military commanders are drawing up plans for a faster withdrawal of American troops from
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; iraq.=&quot;Iraq.&quot;&gt;
  Iraq
 &lt;/a&gt;
 in anticipation that President-elect
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama=&quot;Obama&quot;&gt;
  Barack Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 will reject current proposals as too slow, Pentagon and military officials said Wednesday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;promo&quot;&gt;
   Blog
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs/thecaucus/thecaucus75.jpg&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; alt=&quot;The&quot; caucus=&quot;Caucus&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; class=&quot;callout&quot; style=&quot;margin-left:&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;h5&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     The Caucus
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h5&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
    The latest on the presidential transition and other news from Washington and around the nation.
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     Join the discussion.
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;ul class=&quot;refer&quot; style=&quot;font-size:75%&quot;&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://elections.nytimes.com/2008/results/president/votes.html&quot;&gt;
     Election Results
    &lt;/a&gt;
    |
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/pages/politics/index.html&quot;&gt;
     More Politics News
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
  &lt;/ul&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;singleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The new plans would provide alternatives to a timetable drawn up by the top American commanders for Iraq to bring troops home more slowly than Mr. Obama promised during his presidential campaign. Those plans were described to Mr. Obama last month.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The officials said that Mr. Obama had not requested the new plans, but that they were being prepared in response to public statements from the president-elect and on the basis of conversations between military officials and members of Mr. Obamas
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/us/series/the_new_team/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; potential=&quot;potential&quot; members=&quot;members&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; president-elect=&quot;President-elect&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama=&quot;Obama&quot;&gt;
  transition team
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama met last week in Washington with his national security team, including
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the defense secretary, and Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A drawdown in Iraq is seen as a prerequisite to any significant American military buildup in Afghanistan, where Mr. Obama is ready to add up to 30,000 troops over the next two years, a near doubling of the current American force there of about 31,000.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The broad outlines of the military plan for Iraq presented to Mr. Obama in December envisioned withdrawing two brigades, or some 7,000 to 8,000 troops, over the next six months, officials said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 American military officials have declined to be more specific about other details in that plan, by Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot;&gt;
  David H. Petraeus
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/ray_odierno/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ray=&quot;Ray&quot; odierno.=&quot;Odierno.&quot;&gt;
  Ray Odierno
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the top American commanders responsible for Iraq. But they have made clear that the plan does  not set forth as fast a withdrawal as Mr. Obama pledged during the presidential campaign, when he repeatedly promised to have all combat troops out of Iraq within 16 months of his taking office, or by May 2010.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Officials with Mr. Obamas transition team say he remains committed to that goal, although he has also said he will listen to the recommendations of his commanders. In an interview on Wednesday,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the vice president-elect, said he was not prepared to talk about new troop-level options.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Brooke Anderson, the national security spokeswoman for the Obama transition team, said, We have had briefings from the Bush administration, including Secretary Gates and Admiral Mullen, about current plans for Iraq and Afghanistan, and we appreciate the information that has been shared. Ms. Anderson said that as president Mr. Obama would meet with his commanders to make a determination to how we move forward to safely redeploy our combat brigades in 16 months.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senior military officers say they have anticipated that Mr. Obama will seek speedier options for Iraq troop withdrawals. But they have also expressed uneasiness about a quick withdrawal from Iraq and are unclear at this point about Mr. Obamas overall strategy in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 It is more than a question of how fast and how low; it includes calculating how much risk you are willing to take in Iraq, one senior military officer said of the discussions over a withdrawal.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The official, who asked not to be identified  because of the delicacy  of discussing war planning before the new commander in chief takes office, said the planning also required defining the future mission for American forces in Iraq and Afghanistan, and goals for where those missions should be in years to come.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Various options are being drawn up to give the new president choices, said another senior military officer involved in the process.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Geoff Morrell, the Pentagon press secretary, said Mr. Gates intended to make sure that Mr. Obama, once he is commander in chief, gets to hear directly from all of the senior military officers with a stake in the Iraq and Afghanistan missions before making any decisions.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The discussions the secretary and the chairman have had with the president-elect and his team have thus far been very broad, Mr. Morrell said. They will not begin the process of presenting the president-elect with specific options for a way ahead in Iraq until after the inauguration.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The current military plan for Iraq was drawn up to meet the recent status-of-forces agreement between the United States and the Iraqi government that calls for both shorter and longer timetables than Mr. Obamas campaign promise. Under that  agreement, all United States combat troops are to be out of Iraqi cities by June and all American forces are to be out of Iraq entirely by the end of 2011. That agreement, however, can be renegotiated.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Even as Mr. Obama prepares for the drawdown in Iraq, some influential Democrats and national security experts have begun voicing concern about his willingness to send up to 30,000 additional American troops to Afghanistan, where the United States has been at war for more than seven years. They say that Mr. Obama has yet to make clear his overall goals beyond calling for more forces, money and diplomacy in an increasingly violent, ungovernable country that the military says presents even more problems than Iraq.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Peter Baker contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/nyt_author_id&gt;

<node id="n1177">
<data key="x">0.0224719101124</data>
<data key="y">0.9</data>
<data key="label">On Iraq, Obama Faces Hard Choices</data>
<data key="date">2009-01-29</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  As
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 moves to redefine the nations mission in Iraq, he faces a difficult choice: Is he willing to abandon a campaign promise or risk a rupture with the military? Or can he finesse the difference?
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sectionPromo&quot;&gt;
   &lt;!--reach of war bug --&gt;
   &lt;h3 class=&quot;promo&quot;&gt;
    Reach of War
   &lt;/h3&gt;
   &lt;a class=&quot;more&quot; href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/pages/world/worldspecial/index.html&quot;&gt;
    Go to Complete Coverage
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;br /&gt;
   &lt;br /&gt;
   &lt;!--baghdad bureau promo --&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;

     &lt;a href=&quot;http://baghdadbureau.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs/baghdadbureau/baghdadbureau163b.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;Baghdad&quot; bureau=&quot;Bureau&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h5&gt;
    &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
     A

     &lt;/a&gt;
     looking at daily life inside Iraq, produced by The Timess Baghdad bureau.
    &lt;/p&gt;
    &lt;a class=&quot;more&quot; href=&quot;http://baghdadbureau.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     Go to the Blog
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;promo&quot;&gt;
   Blog
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs/thecaucus/thecaucus75.jpg&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; alt=&quot;The&quot; caucus=&quot;Caucus&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; class=&quot;callout&quot; style=&quot;margin-left:&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;h5&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     The Caucus
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h5&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
    The latest on President Obama, the new administration and other news from Washington and around the nation.
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     Join the discussion.
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;ul class=&quot;refer&quot; style=&quot;font-size:75%&quot;&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://elections.nytimes.com/2008/results/president/votes.html&quot;&gt;
     Election Results
    &lt;/a&gt;
    |
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/pages/politics/index.html&quot;&gt;
     More Politics News
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
  &lt;/ul&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;singleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/01/29/world/29prexy02-190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;195&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    Michael Kamber for The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    Gen. Ray Odierno, the top commander in Iraq, met with American soldiers on Wednesday in Jisr Diyala, south of Baghdad.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Since taking office last week, Mr. Obama has recommitted to ending the war in Iraq but not to his specific campaign pledge to pull out roughly one combat brigade a month for the first 16 months of his presidency. His top commander in Iraq has proposed a slower start to the withdrawal, warning of the dangers of drawing down too quickly.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 On Wednesday, Mr. Obama visited the Pentagon for the first time since becoming president, and he seemed to be looking for an option that would let him stay true to his campaign promise, at least in theory, without alienating the generals. The White House indicated that Mr. Obama was open to alternatives to his 16-month time frame and emphasized that security was an important factor in his decision.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Were no longer involved in a debate about whether, but how and when,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_gibbs/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; gibbs.=&quot;Gibbs.&quot;&gt;
  Robert Gibbs
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the White House press secretary, said about a withdrawal from Iraq. Thats a process the president wants to take seriously.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He added: He wants to ensure the safety of our troops as we remove our combat brigades; wants to, as Ive said repeatedly, provide the responsibility and the opportunity for the Iraqis to do more in governing their own country; and, as I said, to do this in a way that seeks the consultation of all those leaders.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Among those consulted by the president was Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/ray_odierno/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ray=&quot;Ray&quot; odierno.=&quot;Odierno.&quot;&gt;
  Ray Odierno
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the top commander in Iraq, who has developed a plan that would move slower than Mr. Obamas campaign timetable, by pulling out two brigades over the next six months. In an interview in Iraq on Wednesday, General Odierno suggested that it might take the rest of the year to determine exactly when United States forces could be drawn down significantly.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I believe that if we can get through the next year peacefully, with incidents about what they are today or better, I think were getting close to enduring stability, which enables us to really reduce, General Odierno said as he inspected a polling center south of Baghdad in advance of provincial elections on Saturday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 General Odierno said the period between this weekends elections and the national elections to be held about a year from now would be critical to determining the future of Iraq. While some American forces could be withdrawn before then, he suggested that the bulk of any pullout would probably come after that.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 We are going to reduce forces this year, the general said. Its the right time to reduce our forces here. I believe that Iraqis are making progress. Its time for us in some places to step back and give them more control. He added, What we want to do is to slowly shift our mission from one thats focused on counterinsurgency to one thats more focused on stability operations.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 After a session at the White House last week, with General Odierno participating via secure video, Mr. Obama traveled to the Pentagon on Wednesday to meet with the service chiefs. The discussion ranged beyond Iraq and Afghanistan, covering a variety of challenges confronting the armed forces. It was a very elevated conversation about the situation worldwide and the threats that we face and the risks that exist around the globe, said Geoff Morrell, the Defense Department spokesman.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Speaking with reporters afterward, Mr. Obama expressed concern about the enormous pressure on our military to carry out a whole set of missions and promised to advance all aspects of American power to make sure that theyre not carrying the full load. He indicated that he had not decided on his approach to Iraq. Were going to have some difficult decisions that were going to have to make surrounding Iraq and Afghanistan, most immediately, Mr. Obama  said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 J. D. Crouch II, who was President Bushs deputy national security adviser and a leading architect of the surge  strategy, said Mr. Obama and his team would be wise to heed the military. They dont want Iraq to go bad because they have too many other important things to do, he said. They dont want to alienate the military. And theres something to be said that the guy who got things under control over there, Ray Odierno, probably has a good idea of what he needs.
&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Peter Baker reported from Washington, and Alissa J. Rubin from Baghdad. Thom Shanker contributed reporting from Washington.
  &lt;/p&gt;

<node id="n1837">
<data key="x">0.117174959872</data>
<data key="y">0.9</data>
<data key="label">Obama Favoring Mid-2010 Pullout in Iraq, Aides Say</data>
<data key="date">2009-02-25</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 is nearing a decision that would order American combat forces out of Iraq by August 2010 as he seeks to finally end a war that has consumed and polarized the United States for nearly six years, senior administration officials said Tuesday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The timetable would give the military three months more to withdraw than the 16-month pullout Mr. Obama promised last year on the campaign trail. Officials said he was prepared to make that shift because he agreed with the concerns of ground commanders who wanted more time to cement security gains, strengthen political institutions and make sure Iraq did not become more  unstable again.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Even with the withdrawal order, Mr. Obama plans to leave behind a residual force of tens of thousands of troops to continue training Iraqi security forces, hunt down foreign terrorist cells and guard American institutions,  as he said he would during last years campaign.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama, who met with Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 on Tuesday, has not made a final decision but could complete his review and announce his plan this week, administration officials said. In his speech to Congress on Tuesday night, Mr. Obama said only that he would soon announce a way forward in Iraq that leaves Iraq to its people and responsibly ends this war.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 It was not clear on Tuesday exactly how many of the 140,000 troops would remain in Iraq after August 2010 or whether any of the 14 combat brigades now there would  stay under a new mission.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The 19-month time frame for the withdrawal of combat troops was first reported Tuesday by The Associated Press. The approach split the difference with military commanders who proposed a range of options, including the 16-month withdrawal Mr. Obama promised last year and a  longer timetable that would have spread the withdrawal over 23 months. Mr. Obamas advisers said they believed they had reached an accommodation that would satisfy both the military and a public eager to get out of Iraq, while relieving the strain on the armed forces and freeing up resources for Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The president has been struck by the fact that there has been a meeting of the minds in a lot of ways among his military advisers about what would be a safe and responsible way to redeploy our troops while protecting our interests in Iraq, said a senior administration official, who spoke on the condition of anonymity because no decision had been announced.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Another top official said the White House was confident that those who supported Mr. Obamas election would accept a somewhat longer  time frame. Hes always said that he would consult with his military commanders on this and would reach a responsible, appropriate decision, the official said. This is not a very large deviation.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The troop withdrawal could also help to ease the budget pressure the White House is facing as Mr. Obama seeks to make good on a promise to cut the federal deficit in half by 2013, when his current term will end.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In recent weeks, Mr. Gates and Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , discussed the three withdrawal options  16, 19 and 23 months  with the president. Pentagon officials characterized the talks as extensive and said that each option was presented with what Mr. Gates and Admiral Mullen saw as the accompanying risks.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Both Mr. Gates and Admiral Mullen made their own recommendations to the president about what they saw as the best option, but Pentagon officials declined to specify them. One senior defense official did say that Mr. Gates has historically always been extremely deferential to his commanders in the field.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The top two commanders responsible for Iraq, Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot;&gt;
  David H. Petraeus
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/ray_odierno/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ray=&quot;Ray&quot; odierno.=&quot;Odierno.&quot;&gt;
  Ray Odierno
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , have declined to say what options they preferred, but military officials have made it clear that the two were uncomfortable with the 16-month plan  that Mr. Obama backed during the campaign.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Pentagon officials said Tuesday that they did not know what the size of the residual force in Iraq might be, although one of Mr. Obamas national security advisers said during the campaign that it could number 30,000 to 55,000 troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Similarly, defense officials said they did not know how many combat troops would stay behind in new missions as trainers, advisers or counterterrorism forces, at least some of whom would still be effectively in combat roles. Military planners have said that in order to meet withdrawal deadlines, they would reassign some combat troops to training and support of the Iraqis, even though the troops would still be armed and go on combat patrols with their Iraqi counterparts.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Administration officials said it was possible that Mr. Obama would announce his decision on Iraq  withdrawals on Friday during a visit to North Carolina, possibly at either Camp Lejeune or Fort Bragg. Camp Lejeune is the home of some 8,000
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/m/us_marine_corps/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; united=&quot;United&quot; states=&quot;States&quot; marine=&quot;Marine&quot; corps=&quot;Corps&quot;&gt;
  Marines
 &lt;/a&gt;
 who are to be deployed to Afghanistan  under a plan Mr. Obama announced last week to send 17,000 more troops to the country.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;
&lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n1870">
<data key="x">0.211878009631</data>
<data key="y">0.4</data>
<data key="label">Obamas Iraq Plan Has December Elections as Turning Point for Pullout</data>
<data key="date">2009-02-26</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s planned Iraq troop drawdown would leave the bulk of American forces in place until early next year while some combat units would remain in place in new roles even beyond a declared August 2010 target for withdrawal, administration officials said Wednesday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The plan would maintain relatively high troop levels through Iraqs parliamentary elections, to be held in December, before beginning in earnest to meet the August 2010 target for removing combat forces, the officials said. Even after August 2010, as many as 50,000 of the 142,000 troops now in Iraq would remain, including some combat units reassigned as Advisory Training Brigades or Advisory Assistance Brigades, the administration and Pentagon officials said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama consistently said during his campaign that he would leave a residual force for training, protection and counterterrorism missions. But the gradual pace of his withdrawal  spread out over 19 months, instead of the 16 months he promised during the campaign  and the possible size of the remaining force left some Democrats discouraged, while some Republicans cautioned against moving too quickly. The administration  intends to call those remaining troops a transition force.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I dont know what the justification is for 50,000, Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/nancy_pelosi/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nancy=&quot;Nancy&quot; pelosi.=&quot;Pelosi.&quot;&gt;
  Nancy Pelosi
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , a California Democrat and the House speaker, said on MSNBC. Noting that she wanted to hear the presidents plan, she added, I would think a third of that, maybe 20,000, a little more than a third, 15,000 or 20,000.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Her Republican counterpart, Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/john_a_boehner/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; boehner.=&quot;Boehner.&quot;&gt;
  John A. Boehner
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of Ohio, said Mr. Obamas plan might not be realistic and compared it to the presidents decision to close the American detention center in Cuba even though the details would take a year to work out.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 What we dont need is another Guantnamo decision that may fly in the face of the facts on the ground, Mr. Boehner told reporters. While it may have sounded good during the campaign, I do think its important that we listen to those commanders and our diplomats who are there to understand how fragile the situation is.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama plans to seek more money for wars in Iraq and Afghanistan from a separate fund outside the Pentagons base budget, which will also grow beyond the 2009 spending plan of $513 billion. The separate war costs budget proposal for 2010 could reach $130 billion to $140 billion, officials said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The officials agreed to discuss the withdrawal plan on condition of anonymity in advance of an expected announcement by Mr. Obama during a trip on Friday to Camp Lejeune, N.C. The planned drawdown reflects an attempt to balance competing imperatives, including Mr. Obamas campaign promises, the ground commanders desire to maintain flexibility and guard against any fresh escalation  of sectarian violence, and the militarys need to relieve the strain on the armed forces.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Word of Mr. Obamas impending decision generated little of the anger that has flavored the Iraq debate for years. Justin Ruben, executive director of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/m/moveon.org/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; moveon.org=&quot;Moveon.org&quot;&gt;
  MoveOn.org
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , a group that has strongly opposed the war, said activists were willing to give Mr. Obama the benefit of the doubt.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 People have confidence that the president is committed to ending the war, Mr. Ruben said. This is basically what he promised in the election.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/john_mccain/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; mccain.=&quot;McCain.&quot;&gt;
  John McCain
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of Arizona, the former Republican presidential candidate and a strong supporter of the war, did not take direct issue with Mr. Obamas plan on Wednesday, but noted that there was a huge caveat in the tens of thousands of troops who would be left behind.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Lets also be realistic, Mr. McCain said. Advisers in any conflict are in harms way.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , without discussing details, said the drawdown would satisfy public hunger to begin ending the war. I think the American people will be  understand exactly what were doing and theyll be pleased, he said on
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/business/companies/nbc_universal/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nbc=&quot;NBC&quot; universal.=&quot;Universal.&quot;&gt;
  NBC
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s Today show. Were keeping a campaign commitment.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The withdrawal would start slowly, with 2 of the 14 American combat brigades now in Iraq pulling out before the December elections, officials said. After the transition to a new government, the withdrawal would accelerate early next year.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The commanders are concerned about maximizing their numbers on the ground for as long as possible, at least until we get to the other side of the elections, another senior official said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Officers warned that even as overall troop levels dropped, there would be fresh American units deploying to Iraq, both to replace those whose tours end and to reshape the force into one better suited for training and advising Iraqis. While most of the troops remaining after August 2010 would be in support roles, some would still be serving in combat as they conducted counterterrorism missions.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I think a limited number of those that remain will conduct combat operations against terrorists, assisting Iraqi security forces, said Geoff Morrell, the Pentagon press secretary, summarizing past descriptions of the new mission offered by  administration and Defense Department officials.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Thats a limited number, a very limited number. But by and large, youre talking about people who we would classify as enablers, support troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;
&lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n1898">
<data key="x">0.30658105939</data>
<data key="y">0.4</data>
<data key="label">With Pledges to Troops and Iraqis, Obama Details Pullout</data>
<data key="date">2009-02-27</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 CAMP LEJEUNE, N.C.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 declared Friday that the United States has now begun the work of ending this war in
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; iraq.=&quot;Iraq.&quot;&gt;
  Iraq
 &lt;/a&gt;
 as he announced the withdrawal of most American forces by the summer of next year while leaving behind as many as 50,000 troops for more limited missions.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;

     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/02/27/us/27obama.3-190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;224&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;

   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    Marines at Camp Lejeune listening to President Obamas speech on Friday.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sidebarArticles&quot;&gt;

     Text: Obamas Speech at Camp Lejeune, N.C.

     U.S. Soldiers in Iraq React
    &lt;/a&gt;
    (February 28, 2009)
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--Article Comments Include--&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/02/27/us/27obam.190.ms.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;149&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    Doug Mills/The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    My highest priority will be the safety and security of our troops and civilians in Iraq, President Obama said at Camp Lejeune, N.C., on Friday.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Nearly six years after American troops crossed the border into Iraq to topple
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/h/saddam_hussein/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; saddam=&quot;Saddam&quot; hussein.=&quot;Hussein.&quot;&gt;
  Saddam Hussein
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Mr. Obama said renewed cause for hope produced by improved security would allow Americans to begin disentangling militarily and turn the country over to the Iraqis themselves.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Let me say this as plainly as I can, the president told thousands of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/m/us_marine_corps/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; united=&quot;United&quot; states=&quot;States&quot; marine=&quot;Marine&quot; corps=&quot;Corps&quot;&gt;
  Marines
 &lt;/a&gt;
 stationed here. By August 31, 2010, our combat mission in Iraq will end.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The transitional force he will leave behind will no longer participate in major combat missions but instead train and advise Iraqi security forces, hunt down terrorist cells and protect American civilian and military personnel working in Iraq. Mr. Obama promised that all of them will leave as well by December 2011 in accordance with a security agreement with Iraq negotiated by President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot;&gt;
  George W. Bush
 &lt;/a&gt;
 before he left office last month.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 At the same time, Mr. Obama vowed to continue the American commitment to building a new Iraqi society and to resettling millions of displaced Iraqis still away from home  elsewhere in their own nation or in neighboring countries. And he promised to escalate diplomatic involvement in the broader region, including new lines of communication with Iran and Syria.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Every nation and every group must know  whether you wish America good or ill  that the end of the war in Iraq will enable a new era of American leadership and engagement in the Middle East, the president said. And that era has just begun.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The announcement marked a sharp turning point in the American venture in Iraq, one that signaled a shift in the once-fiery political debate at home and in the nations priorities abroad. The choice of Camp Lejeune, the largest Marine base on the East Coast, symbolized the transition because 8,000 troops from here will soon ship out to Afghanistan as part of a 17,000-troop buildup ordered by Mr. Obama.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The reaction to the Iraq drawdown plan indicated an emerging consensus in the United States that it is time to begin getting out. While some leading Congressional Democrats grumbled about the size of the residual force, the drawdown largely won support across party lines, including from leading Republicans like Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/john_mccain/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; mccain.=&quot;McCain.&quot;&gt;
  John McCain
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of Arizona, who lost years election to Mr. Obama after a fierce debate over Iraq.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Speaking on the Senate floor on Friday before the presidents speech, Mr. McCain credited the opportunity to pull troops out to the surge that Mr. Bush ordered two years ago with his support. But he cautioned that Iraq remains fragile, urging Mr. Obama to remain flexible and listen to military commanders.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 With these factors in mind, I believe the presidents withdrawal plan is a reasonable one, Mr. McCain said. Given the gains in Iraq and the requirements to send additional troops to Afghanistan, together with the significant number of troops that will remain in Iraq and the presidents willingness to reassess based on conditions on the ground, I am cautiously optimistic that the plan as laid out by the president can lead to success.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Former Bush aides also offered support for the plan, calling it the logical next step after the presidents agreement with Iraq to withdraw all forces by the end of 2011. The specific timing is only slightly different but consistent with the goal of helping Iraq become self sufficient in providing its own security, Gordon D. Johndroe, who was Mr. Bushs last national security spokesman, said in an interview. This is possible because of the success of the surge.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama called Mr. Bush from a holding room at Camp Lejeune just before going on stage in the base gymnasium to make the announcement, aides said. He called Prime Minister
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/nuri_kamal_al-maliki/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nuri=&quot;Nuri&quot; kamal=&quot;Kamal&quot; al-maliki.=&quot;al-Maliki.&quot;&gt;
  Nuri Kamal al-Maliki
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of Iraq from
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/p/presidents_and_presidency_us/air_force_one/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; air=&quot;Air&quot; force=&quot;Force&quot; one.=&quot;One.&quot;&gt;
  Air Force One
 &lt;/a&gt;
 on the flight from Washington to brief him on the withdrawal plan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In Baghdad, Yassen Majeed, an adviser to Mr. Maliki, said the prime minister is very comfortable with the plan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The Prime Minister assured the American president that the security situation in Iraq is stable and his forces are ready to take over all the responsibilities from the American side.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But others there were more cautious, including Sunni lawmakers worried about their the possible erosion of their influence in the Shiite-dominated government.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Several noted with approval Mr. Obamas statement that the Iraqi government would only have American support as long as it remained non-sectarian. All Iraqis want the American to withdraw from Iraq as soon as possible, said Adnan al-Dulaimi, a senior Sunni politician. Were just afraid of the vacuum that this withdrawal may cause.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 During his speech, Mr. Obama credited troops who got the job done but gave no credit to the troop surge and associated strategy shift that he opposed in January 2007. He praised Ambassador
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/ryan_c_crocker/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ryan=&quot;Ryan&quot; c.=&quot;C.&quot; crocker.=&quot;Crocker.&quot;&gt;
  Ryan Crocker
 &lt;/a&gt;
 as an unsung hero and Gens.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot;&gt;
  David H. Petraeus
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/ray_odierno/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ray=&quot;Ray&quot; odierno.=&quot;Odierno.&quot;&gt;
  Ray Odierno
 &lt;/a&gt;
 as the finest generals, without mentioning Mr. Bush. His only implicit reference to his predecessor came when he said Iraq had taught painful lessons about how and when America should go to war.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;pageLinks&quot;&gt;
 &lt;ul id=&quot;pageNumbers&quot;&gt;
  &lt;li&gt;
   1
  &lt;/li&gt;
  &lt;li&gt;
   &lt;a onclick=&quot;s_code_linktrack(&quot;&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;/li&gt;
 &lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Mark Santora contributed reporting from Baghdad.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;

&lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n4276">
<data key="x">0.401284109149</data>
<data key="y">0.5</data>
<data key="label">Afghan Valley Offers Test for Obama Strategy</data>
<data key="date">2009-06-01</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 JALREZ BAZAAR,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; afghanistan.=&quot;Afghanistan.&quot;&gt;
  Afghanistan
 &lt;/a&gt;
 A year ago, the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 were tormenting this lush valley just miles from the Afghan capital, kidnapping people and blocking the road.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sidebarArticles&quot;&gt;
   &lt;h4&gt;
    Related
   &lt;/h4&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/06/01/world/asia/01afghan.html?ref=asia&quot;&gt;
     U.S. and Taliban to Redouble Afghan Efforts
    &lt;/a&gt;
    (June 1, 2009)
   &lt;/h2&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    Times Topics:
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html&quot;&gt;
     Afghanistan
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/06/01/world/jalrez_map190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;133&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    Jalrez may be an indicator of the benefit of additional troops.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 All that changed when American troops arrived in February. They dropped from helicopters and set up three camps where there had been none, expecting a fight. Instead, the Taliban put up almost no resistance and left for other areas. Now trucks travel freely and merchants no longer fear for their lives.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Compared with last year, its 100 percent different, said Muhamed Zaker, an apple farmer from the area.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The Jalrez Valley is a test case, the first area in Afghanistan where
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s strategy of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/03/26/washington/28prexy.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; article=&quot;article&quot; on=&quot;on&quot; president=&quot;President&quot; obamas=&quot;Obamas&quot; strategy=&quot;strategy&quot;&gt;
  increasing troop levels
 &lt;/a&gt;
 has been applied, and it is a promising early indicator.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But in Afghanistan, a complex patchwork of tribes, ethnicities and rivalries, it remains unclear whether the early success in this area  can be replicated. In the painstaking business of counterinsurgency, security requires more than just extra troops. It means giving Afghans reasons to reject the insurgents by providing the basic trappings of a state  an effective police force, enough government services, and economic opportunity so they can work rather than fight.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 has said the troops here have about a year to show they can turn around the momentum of the war, before Afghan and American patience runs out.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But Afghanistan is a country where only a third of the population can read and even the most rudimentary infrastructure is lacking, and commanders on the ground say rushing the process would be a mistake.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Its construction, not
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/reconstruction/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; reconstruction=&quot;reconstruction&quot; effort=&quot;effort&quot; in=&quot;in&quot; iraq.=&quot;Iraq.&quot;&gt;
  reconstruction
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , one American officer said, comparing the task with that in Iraq, where the American effort was referred to as reconstruction.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 One problem is that the gains in Jalrez could still be temporary. Insurgents regularly leave areas where Americans appear, only to resurface later. We are hearing its better now, said Hoji Mir Ahmad, a fruit merchant based in Kabul, but God knows what things will be like when the harvest comes.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 When the Americans came to the Jalrez Valley, a skinny finger of green just 30 miles west of Kabul, the capital, Taliban fighters had controlled it for more than a year, taking advantage of a virtual absence of American troops. A unit of about 200 American soldiers had patrolled an area of half a million people and was so thinly spread that its captain had to drive 12 hours to hold a meeting with a local leader.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Humiliations had become routine: The Taliban would blacken the faces of men they said were thieves and parade them. In Jalrez Bazaar, a town west of the valley, eight people were killed in 2008,  residents said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 It looked like we didnt have any destiny, said Momin Shah, a farmer, sitting on a crate in a small supply shop.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Fearing that the Taliban were tightening their hold around Kabul, the Americans were sent to secure the two provinces just south and west of it, Logar and Wardak, the gateway to the capital and the location of the countrys main north-south highway.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Then came the first surprise: The Taliban left for other areas rather than fight. Musa Hotak, a member of Parliament from Jalrez District who is a former Taliban commander, said the two main militant leaders had moved with their families to Pakistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The reason, American officers said, was simple math. The new contingent increased the number of  Americans tenfold. Mass counts, said Lt. Col. Kimo Gallahue, a commander in the new battalion.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 What is now causing unrest in Jalrez is an assortment of low-level criminals, Americans and Afghans said, men who may be thought of as Taliban, but whose main pursuit is money, not infidels. (The main target in Jalrez is a man whose last big crime was stealing solar panels.) That gives the Americans hope that if they bring money and jobs fast enough here and to the rest country, they could substantially weaken the insurgency.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I learned everything I know about the Jalrez insurgency from
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.hbo.com/sopranos/&quot; title=&quot;Sopranos&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
  The Sopranos
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Colonel Gallahue said. At the foot soldier level, its economically driven.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 For Afghans, life has improved, a fact that, for Jalrez Bazaar residents, has trumped the irritation at having foreign troops on Afghan soil. People hate them but its better to have them here, said Shah Mahmoud, a farmer, 70. If security is established, we dont need the Americans and they dont need us.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In the rules of counterinsurgency, soldiers must move quickly  but carefully  to solidify gains.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The Americans are trying to strike a delicate balance between wooing villagers with public works projects and continuing to put pressure on insurgents in the same areas.  Progress is slow.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;pageLinks&quot;&gt;
 &lt;ul id=&quot;pageNumbers&quot;&gt;

  &lt;/li&gt;

   &lt;a onclick=&quot;s_code_linktrack(&quot;&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;/li&gt;
 &lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;

 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Abdul Waheed Wafa contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;

<node id="n5197">
<data key="x">0.495987158909</data>
<data key="y">0.7</data>
<data key="label">In Speech, Obama Cites Common U.S.- Russian Interests</data>
<data key="date">2009-07-07</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 MOSCOW
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 said on Tuesday that America and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/russiaandtheformersovietunion/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; russia=&quot;Russia&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; post-soviet=&quot;Post-Soviet&quot; nations.=&quot;Nations.&quot;&gt;
  Russia
 &lt;/a&gt;
 share common interests in building a secure, free and flourishing world but rejected complaints about American support for missile defense and expansion of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 alliance into Eastern Europe.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sidebarArticles&quot;&gt;
   &lt;h4&gt;
    Related
   &lt;/h4&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/07/07/world/europe/07ruble.html?ref=europe&quot;&gt;
     Business Deals in Moscow Meetings Shadow
    &lt;/a&gt;
    (July 7, 2009)
   &lt;/h2&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;h3 class=&quot;promo&quot;&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/07/06/russia-and-the-perils-of-personal-diplomacy&quot;&gt;
      Russia and the Perils of Personal Diplomacy
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h3&gt;
    &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/07/06/russia-and-the-perils-of-personal-diplomacy&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/roomfordebate/roomfordebate75.gif&quot; alt=&quot;Room&quot; for=&quot;for&quot; debate=&quot;Debate&quot; class=&quot;callout&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
     Should President Obama try to bond with President Medvedev, or have such ties with Russian leaders hurt U.S. interests?
    &lt;/p&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/07/06/russia-and-the-perils-of-personal-diplomacy/&quot; class=&quot;more&quot;&gt;
     &lt;strong&gt;
      Post a Comment
     &lt;/strong&gt;
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--hasEmbeddedPlayer promo include for articles --&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/07/07/world/07prexy.inline.190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;127&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    James Hill for The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    Waiters at the Kremlin photographed a live television image of President Obama on Monday as he met with his Russian counterpart, Dmitri A. Medvedev.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;!--calling embedded video jsp --&gt;
&lt;!--brightcove player begins --&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;inlineVideo&quot; left=&quot;left&quot; brightcove=&quot;brightcove&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--NYT video player embed code *starts here* - Build# 2008.09.17 --&gt;
 &lt;!--NYT video player embed code *ends here* --&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;!--brightcove player ends --&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In a speech intended to highlight his two-day visit, Mr. Obama reached out to national sensibilities here by assuring that American wants a strong, peaceful and prosperous Russia and declaring that it is not for me to define Russias national interests.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Yet he made the case that Russia should join America in curbing emerging nuclear powers like Iran and in promoting greater liberties at home.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 By no means is America perfect, the president said in a speech at the New Economic School, a graduate school in Moscow formed after the fall of the Soviet Union to introduce modern market economics to Russia. But it is our commitment to certain universal values which allows us to correct our imperfections and to grow stronger over time.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He added: If our democracy did not advance those rights, I  as a person of African ancestry  wouldnt be able to address you as an American citizen, much less a president.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obamas speech came one day after he signed an agreement in principle with President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/dmitri_a_medvedev/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; dmitri=&quot;Dmitri&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; medvedev.=&quot;Medvedev.&quot;&gt;
  Dmitri A. Medvedev
 &lt;/a&gt;
 to cut Russian and American strategic nuclear arsenals by at least one-quarter.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 As he began his second day in Moscow, Mr. Obama had breakfast with Prime Minister
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/vladimir_v_putin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; vladimir=&quot;Vladimir&quot; v.=&quot;V.&quot; putin.=&quot;Putin.&quot;&gt;
  Vladimir V. Putin
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , widely viewed as Russias paramount leader, in a meeting that ran long over its scheduled time. Speaking to reporters beforehand, Mr. Putin noted that there have been periods of grayish mood between our two countries, an allusion to the tension of recent years that culminated with last years war between Russia and its small neighbor, Georgia.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 With you, Mr. Putin told Mr. Obama, we link all our hopes for the furtherance of relations between our two countries.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Neither man made any public mention of Mr. Obamas comment in an interview last week that Mr. Putin still has one foot in the old ways of doing business. Instead, Mr. Obama lavished praise on Mr. Putin, while stumbling for the second time in as many days over his titles. Im aware of not only the extraordinary work that youve done on behalf of the Russian people in your previous role as prime minister  as president, but in your current role as prime minister.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama came here in hopes of rebuilding relations with Russia after they frayed under his predecessor, President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot;&gt;
  George W. Bush
 &lt;/a&gt;
 . In addition to the nuclear arms agreement, he and Mr. Medvedev sealed a deal allowing the American military to send thousands of flights of troops and weapons to Afghanistan through Russian airspace each year and they renewed military contacts suspended after last years Georgia war.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The two did not reach a trade deal the Obama administration once hoped for, and made no progress in bridging the divide over American plans to build a missile defense system in Eastern Europe. But Mr. Medvedev was pleased that Mr. Obama agreed that they should talk about both offensive and defensive weapons and the American president was pleased that his Russian counterpart agreed to conduct a joint review of any Iranian nuclear threat.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama mapped out his second day in part to demonstrate continuing American support for democracy and rule of law in Russia.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He met Tuesday morning with
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/mikhail_s_gorbachev/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; mikhail=&quot;Mikhail&quot; s.=&quot;S.&quot; gorbachev.=&quot;Gorbachev.&quot;&gt;
  Mikhail S. Gorbachev
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the former Soviet president who ushered in glasnost and the changes that ultimately unraveled the Soviet Union. Mr. Obama also planned to meet later in the day with business leaders and opposition leaders and attend a conference on civil society. Mr. Medvedev was also invited to the civil society event but declined.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obamas speech at the New Economic School was calculated to address longstanding Russian grievances against America, which many here suspect still seeks to hold Russia down, interfere in its internal affairs and extend its influence into its backyard. But the speech was not carried on any of the major Russian television networks, all of which are controlled by the state.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama did not paper over major policy differences and instead argued that Russia should not fear American intentions. Neither America nor Russia would benefit from a nuclear arms race in East Asia or the Middle East, he said. That is why we should be united in opposing North Koreas efforts to become a nuclear power, and preventing Iran from acquiring a nuclear weapon.
&lt;/p&gt;

<node id="n5651">
<data key="x">0.590690208668</data>
<data key="y">0.4</data>
<data key="label">Iraq Premier and Obama Emphasize the Positive</data>
<data key="date">2009-07-23</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 welcomed Prime Minister
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/nuri_kamal_al-maliki/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nuri=&quot;Nuri&quot; kamal=&quot;Kamal&quot; al-maliki.=&quot;al-Maliki.&quot;&gt;
  Nuri Kamal al-Maliki
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; iraq.=&quot;Iraq.&quot;&gt;
  Iraq
 &lt;/a&gt;
 to the White House on Wednesday and said that despite occasional differences between the two nations military forces, the United States was on track for
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/02/26/washington/26troops.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  withdrawing combat forces
 &lt;/a&gt;
 from Iraq by the end of August 2010.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/07/23/world/23prexy.190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;234&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    Brendan Smialowski for The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    President Obama and Prime Minister Nuri Kamal al-Maliki listening to a reporters question in the Rose Garden.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--hasEmbeddedPlayer promo include for articles --&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;!--calling embedded video jsp --&gt;
&lt;!--brightcove player begins --&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;inlineVideo&quot; left=&quot;left&quot; brightcove=&quot;brightcove&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--NYT video player embed code *starts here* - Build# 2008.09.17 --&gt;
 &lt;!--NYT video player embed code *ends here* --&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;!--brightcove player ends --&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The United States and Iraq have known difficult times together, Mr. Obama said. Now, both of us agree that the bonds forged between Americans and Iraqis in war can pave the way for progress that can be forged in peace.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.whitehouse.gov/the_press_office/Remarks-of-President-Obama-and-Prime-Minister-Maliki-of-Iraq-in-Joint-Press-Availability/&quot; title=&quot;White&quot; house=&quot;House&quot; transcript=&quot;transcript&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; remarks=&quot;remarks&quot; by=&quot;by&quot; mr.=&quot;Mr.&quot; obama=&quot;Obama&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; mr.=&quot;Mr.&quot; maliki=&quot;Maliki&quot;&gt;
  a joint appearance in the Rose Garden
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the two leaders sidestepped some of the recent conflicts over details of the withdrawal and security, and they presented a positive portrait of the evolving relationship between the United States and Iraq. Although Mr. Obama conceded there would be some tough days ahead, he said he remained confident that the Iraqi forces would ultimately be able to handle much of their own security so the United States could pull out its combat troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The president also said he was committed to working with Iraq to persuade the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/u/united_nations/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; united=&quot;United&quot; nations.=&quot;Nations.&quot;&gt;
  United Nations
 &lt;/a&gt;
 to ease international sanctions imposed on Iraq after the 1991 Persian Gulf war. The sanctions, which were imposed on
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/h/saddam_hussein/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; saddam=&quot;Saddam&quot; hussein.=&quot;Hussein.&quot;&gt;
  Saddam Hussein
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s government, require Iraq to pay 5 percent of its oil revenue as war reparations.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 It would be a mistake for Iraq to continue to be burdened by the sins of a deposed dictator, Mr. Obama said, responding to a question from an Iraqi reporter.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Malikis visit to the White House for a series of meetings with Mr. Obama and other administration officials was the highlight of his weeklong trip to the United States. The two leaders met privately in the Oval Office, their first meeting since
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/07/01/world/middleeast/01iraq.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  American forces turned over security in cities and towns to Iraqis
 &lt;/a&gt;
 on June 30.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 From working closely with the American forces and the multinational forces, our forces became highly capable, Mr. Maliki said, speaking through an interpreter. And they will continue to do their role and their part to provide the opportunity needed for
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/reconstruction/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; reconstruction=&quot;reconstruction&quot; effort=&quot;effort&quot; in=&quot;in&quot; iraq.=&quot;Iraq.&quot;&gt;
  reconstruction
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , rebuilding and developing Iraq.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 For the White House, the private meeting with the prime minister was a rare public shift away from health care policy-making, which has dominated the presidents week.  Mr. Obama said the United States was eager to move beyond its military relationship with Iraq to encourage more business investment and stable diplomatic relations. Still, about 130,000 United States troops remain in the country.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Violence continues to be down, and Iraqis are taking responsibility for their future, Mr. Obama said, standing beneath a broiling sun alongside Mr. Maliki. We have been very encouraged by the progress.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Maliki said Iraq needed to build upon a strategic relationship on the economic front. He said Iraq planned to convene an investment conference in October for companies eager to look for business opportunities in the country.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Iraq has suffered a great deal from being marginalized, from the policies of sectarianism and from wars, Mr. Maliki said. We will work very hard not to allow any sectarian behavior and opportunity to flourish.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 On his trip to Washington, the prime minister is also scheduled to meet with
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/treasury_department/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; u.s.=&quot;U.S.&quot; treasury=&quot;Treasury&quot; department.=&quot;Department.&quot;&gt;
  Treasury
 &lt;/a&gt;
 Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/timothy_f_geithner/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; timothy=&quot;Timothy&quot; f.=&quot;F.&quot; geithner.=&quot;Geithner.&quot;&gt;
  Timothy F. Geithner
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and Congressional leaders.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;

<node id="n6870">
<data key="x">0.685393258427</data>
<data key="y">0.8</data>
<data key="label">Advisers to Obama Divided on Size of Afghan Force</data>
<data key="date">2009-09-04</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  The militarys anticipated request for more troops to combat the insurgency in
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; afghanistan.=&quot;Afghanistan.&quot;&gt;
  Afghanistan
 &lt;/a&gt;
 has divided senior advisers to
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 as they try to determine the proper size and mission of the American effort there, officials said Thursday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
