  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/09/04/world/04policy_190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;126&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    Stephen Crowley/The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    Secretary of Defense Robert M. Gates and Adm. Mike Mullen, the chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff, discussed Afghanistan during a news briefing at the Pentagon on Thursday.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;!--calling embedded video jsp --&gt;
&lt;!--brightcove player begins --&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;inlineVideo&quot; left=&quot;left&quot; brightcove=&quot;brightcove&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--NYT video player embed code *starts here* - Build# 2008.09.17 --&gt;
 &lt;!--NYT video player embed code *ends here* --&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;!--brightcove player ends --&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Even before the top commander in Afghanistan submits his proposal for additional forces, administration officials have begun what one called a healthy debate about what the priorities should be and whether more American soldiers and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/m/us_marine_corps/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; united=&quot;United&quot; states=&quot;States&quot; marine=&quot;Marine&quot; corps=&quot;Corps&quot;&gt;
  Marines
 &lt;/a&gt;
 would help achieve them.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Leading those with doubts is Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , who has expressed deep reservations about an expanded presence in Afghanistan on the grounds that it may distract from what he considers the more urgent goal of stabilizing Pakistan, officials said. Among those on the other side are
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/h/richard_c_holbrooke/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; richard=&quot;Richard&quot; c.=&quot;C.&quot; holbrooke.=&quot;Holbrooke.&quot;&gt;
  Richard C. Holbrooke
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the special representative to the region, who shares the concern about Pakistan but sees more troops as vital to protecting Afghan civilians and undermining the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 has been vocal in favor of more troops, and while some officials said she had not shown her hand during the current deliberations, they expected her to be an advocate for a more robust force.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 has voiced concern that putting so many troops in Afghanistan would make the United States look like an occupier, but during a news conference on Thursday he sounded more supportive of the prospect.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 There is a unanimity of opinion about what our objective is, and the objective is to disable and destroy Al Qaeda and remove that threat to our national security, said
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/a/david_axelrod/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; axelrod.=&quot;Axelrod.&quot;&gt;
  David Axelrod
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the presidents senior adviser. Obviously, there are a variety of opinions about how best to achieve that objective, and its valuable and important to hear those views.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The emerging debate follows the delivery Monday of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/09/01/world/asia/01military.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  a new strategic assessment
 &lt;/a&gt;
 by Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , who took over all American and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 forces in Afghanistan in June. Mr. Gates has now forwarded the generals report of about 25 pages to Mr. Obama.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Although General McChrystal included no specific force proposals in his review, officials expect him to send a separate request in the coming weeks. Military strategists, including one who has advised General McChrystal, said he might offer three options. The smallest proposed reinforcement, from 10,000 to 15,000  troops, would be described as the high-risk option. A medium-risk option would involve sending about 25,000 more troops, and a low-risk option would call for sending about 45,000 troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Geoff Morrell, the Pentagon press secretary, cautioned that talk about troop levels was speculation. Anyone who tells you that they know how many troops the commander is going to ask for and the options he may or may not present doesnt know what hes talking about, because that has not been determined yet, Mr. Morrell said. He said that Mr. Gates had not made up his mind about what he would recommend to the president.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Gates could be the key adviser on this decision, and some military analysts predicted that he might recommend what Pentagon officials call the Goldilocks option  the medium-risk one in the middle. Because he was first appointed by President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot;&gt;
  George W. Bush
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Mr. Gates could provide political cover for Mr. Obama should the president reject the biggest possible buildup.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Gates has long been worried that a large number of American forces would alienate the Afghan population. But at a news conference with Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Mr. Gates said Thursday that
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/09/04/us/politics/04military.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  his concerns about the American footprint
 &lt;/a&gt;
 had been mitigated by General McChrystal, who has indicated that the size of the force is less important than what it does.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Where foreign forces have had a large footprint and failed, in no small part it has been because the Afghans concluded they were there for their own imperial interests and not there for the interests of the Afghan people, Mr. Gates said. But he said that General McChrystals emphasis on reducing civilian casualties and interacting more with Afghans has given us a greater margin of error in that respect.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama has already ordered 21,000 additional troops to Afghanistan this year for a total American force of 68,000, on top of 40,000 NATO troops. Mrs. Clinton and Mr. Holbrooke pushed for those reinforcements, while Mr. Biden resisted. It is true that Hillary was very forceful; I had some disagreement in degree with her, Mr. Biden later told USA Today. The president ended up landing on a spot that was where she was.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Biden has argued that a sizable increase in resources for Afghanistan invariably means less for Pakistan, a concern born out of his frustration as a senator during the Bush administration pushing for more aid to Islamabad. In some ways, he has told colleagues, Pakistan is more important than Afghanistan because extremism is on the rise there, Al Qaeda has operating room and the government of Pakistan, a nuclear-armed nation, remains vulnerable.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Other American officials said they worried that General McChrystal simply did not have enough forces to turn around Afghanistan. Mr. Holbrooke just returned from Afghanistan, where he heard from military officers who said they needed more help to execute General McChrystals strategy of protecting the population from the Taliban, rather than just hunting militants.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 As the presidents senior uniformed adviser, Admiral Mullen has said he worries about the impact of a buildup on the nations already stretched armed forces. In July, Mr. Gates announced a temporary increase of 22,000 troops in the size of the Army.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mediating the debate will be Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/j/james_l_jones/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; james=&quot;James&quot; l.=&quot;L.&quot; jones.=&quot;Jones.&quot;&gt;
  James L. Jones
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the national security adviser. My job is to make sure the process works the way the president wants and everybody is at the table, he said. I try to be open-minded and not prejudice anything.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He said he would ensure that dissidents got to voice their views to Mr. Obama. He encourages vigorous debate, General Jones said. The thing not to do in a meeting with the president is to sit on your hands and hope you dont get called on, because thats a guarantee that youre going to get called on.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;
&lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n7041">
<data key="x">0.780096308186</data>
<data key="y">0.5</data>
<data key="label">Obama Facing Doubts Within His Own Party on Afghanistan</data>
<data key="date">2009-09-11</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  The leading Senate Democrat on military matters said Thursday that he was against sending more American combat troops to Afghanistan until the United States speeded up the training and equipping of more Afghan security forces.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sidebarArticles&quot;&gt;
   &lt;h4&gt;
    Related
   &lt;/h4&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    Times Topics:
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/presidency/index.html&quot;&gt;
     The Presidency of Barack Obama
    &lt;/a&gt;
    |
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html&quot;&gt;
     Afghanistan
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The comments by the senator,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/l/carl_levin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; carl=&quot;Carl&quot; levin.=&quot;Levin.&quot;&gt;
  Carl Levin
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , a Michigan Democrat who is the chairman of the Armed Services Committee, illustrate the growing skepticism
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 is facing in his own party as the White House decides whether to commit more deeply to a war that has begun losing public support, even as American commanders acknowledge that the situation on the ground has deteriorated.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator Levins comments, made in an interview and in the draft of a speech he will deliver Friday, are significant because his  stature on military matters gives him the ability to sway fellow lawmakers, and his pivotal committee position provides a platform for vetting Mr. Obamas major decisions on troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Underscoring the increasing unease, the House speaker,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/nancy_pelosi/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nancy=&quot;Nancy&quot; pelosi.=&quot;Pelosi.&quot;&gt;
  Nancy Pelosi
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , said earlier on Thursday that the president would face opposition if he sought to fulfill an expected request from Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the top commander in Afghanistan, for more American combat troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I dont think there is a great deal of support for sending more troops to Afghanistan in the country or in Congress, Ms. Pelosi told reporters, emphasizing that she was eager to see a report due from the White House in two weeks on benchmarks to measure the success of the administrations six-month-old strategy.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The White House has begun to indicate that it could be weeks or perhaps much longer before Mr. Obama decides whether to send more troops to Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Administration officials say they want to do a complete review of the effectiveness of the last  troop increase, which will put the American presence at 68,000 troops by years end, an all-time high. They are also digesting a strategic assessment of the Afghan mission that General McChrystal has submitted.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A delay on deciding whether to increase American troop levels would also have the political advantage of pushing down the road a split within Mr. Obamas party while he is trying to build coalitions for overhauling the health care system.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In the telephone interview on Thursday, Mr. Levin said he was not ruling out sending more troops eventually, but rather insisted that the United States try again on a years-old project: finding a way to expand and accelerate the training of the Afghan security forces.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I just think we should hold off on a commitment to send more combat troops until these additional steps to strengthen the Afghan security forces are put in motion, he said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Levin, who returned from a trip to Afghanistan just last week, said that the Afghan national army should be increased to 240,000 troops by 2012 from a current goal of 134,000 by next year, and that Afghan national police forces should grow to 160,000 officers from 96,800 in the same period. These troop goals are consistent with General McChrystals planning but would be reached a year earlier, the senator said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Levin acknowledged that more American trainers would be needed to meet that goal, but he said that he did not know how many. In the most recent deployment of 21,000 American troops, about 4,000 were trainers. The last of those forces will not be in place until November.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In counterinsurgency operations, there are sometimes few distinctions between trainers, support troops and combat forces, a fact that Mr. Levin said he recognized.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He said the United States should send Afghan  forces more equipment  including rifles, bullets and trucks  and shift more equipment to Afghanistan from stocks now in Iraq.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Finally, Mr. Levin said the administration needed to adopt a plan to separate low-  and midlevel  insurgents from hard-core
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 fighters and commanders. He said the current American efforts to do this had been tentative and halfhearted.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Levin, who said he intended to outline his proposal in a speech on the Senate floor on Friday, said he explained his concerns in meetings on Wednesday with Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Gates has indicated that he is willing to consider a request for more forces. Separate from any troop request forwarded by the commanders in Afghanistan, Mr. Gates has said he will press for more troops and equipment to protect American, allied and Afghan forces from
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/i/improvised_explosive_devices/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; improvised=&quot;improvised&quot; explosive=&quot;explosive&quot; devices.=&quot;devices.&quot;&gt;
  improvised explosive devices
 &lt;/a&gt;
 ,  which are the roadside bombs that have been the leading cause of death and injuries in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Troops for the mission to counter roadside bombs, which potentially could number in the thousands, would include route- clearance teams and ordnance-disposal units  some of the most dangerous jobs in the military  as well as intelligence analysts and medical personnel. They would be in addition to a substantial increase in the number of armored troop transport vehicles sent to Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 While Mr. Levin traveled to Afghanistan last week with two other colleagues, the lawmakers did not agree on all positions.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/r/jack_reed/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; jack=&quot;Jack&quot; reed.=&quot;Reed.&quot;&gt;
  Jack Reed
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , a Rhode Island Democrat, said in an interview that he agreed with the need to speed the training and equipping of the Afghan security forces and to reintegrate any Taliban fighters willing to recognize the Afghan government.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Reed said he was waiting for the analysis by General McChrystal on possible troop increases before making up his mind. What the president has to do is continually point to the fact that
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 is operating in the border areas of Afghanistan and Pakistan, he said. Given the chance to reconstitute themselves and operate in those border spaces, theyll pose a threat to the United States.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Representative Adam Smith, a Washington State Democrat on the House Armed Services and Intelligence Committees who traveled to Afghanistan and Pakistan in the past week, said he also wanted more information before deciding. But my general position is we have to give General McChrystal what he needs to get the job done, he said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Other Democrats said Mr. Obama and his military commanders needed to make a more persuasive case to sell the administrations Afghanistan strategy.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 They have a relatively short period of time to show that were on a path thats going to demonstrate positive results, said Representative Earl Pomeroy, a North Dakota Democrat who visited Afghanistan last week. This is our last best chance to change things around.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Thom Shanker contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;

<node id="n7327">
<data key="x">0.874799357945</data>
<data key="y">0.8</data>
<data key="label">News Analysis: In Afghanistan Assessment, a Catalyst for Obama</data>
<data key="date">2009-09-22</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 could read the grim assessment of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; afghanistan.=&quot;Afghanistan.&quot;&gt;
  Afghanistan
 &lt;/a&gt;
 war from his top military commander there in two possible ways.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sectionPromo&quot;&gt;
   &lt;!--at war promo --&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;h5&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/atwar/atwar190.gif&quot; alt=&quot;At&quot; war=&quot;War&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h5&gt;
    &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
     Notes from Afghanistan, Pakistan, Iraq and other areas of conflict in the post-9/11 era.
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      Go to the Blog
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/p&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sidebarArticles&quot;&gt;
   &lt;h4&gt;
    Related
   &lt;/h4&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/09/21/world/asia/21afghan.html?ref=asia&quot;&gt;
     General Calls for More U.S. Troops to Avoid Afghan Failure
    &lt;/a&gt;
    (September 21, 2009)
   &lt;/h2&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;h3 class=&quot;promo&quot;&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/09/21/fending-off-failure-in-afghanistan&quot;&gt;
      Fending Off Failure in Afghanistan
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h3&gt;
    &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/09/21/fending-off-failure-in-afghanistan&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/roomfordebate/roomfordebate75.gif&quot; alt=&quot;Room&quot; for=&quot;for&quot; debate=&quot;Debate&quot; class=&quot;callout&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
     If more troops are required, how should they be deployed?
    &lt;/p&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/09/21/fending-off-failure-in-afghanistan/&quot; class=&quot;more&quot;&gt;
     &lt;strong&gt;
      Join the Discussion
     &lt;/strong&gt;
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--Article Comments Include--&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He could read
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/09/21/world/asia/21afghan.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  Gen.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s report
 as a blunt and impassioned last-chance plea for a revamped counterinsurgency strategy bolstered by thousands more combat troops to rescue the beleaguered, eight-year mission.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Or he could read it as a searing indictment of American-led
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 military operations and a corrupt Afghan civilian government, pitted against a surprisingly adaptive and increasingly dangerous insurgency.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Either way, General McChrystals 66-page report with the deceptively bland title Commanders Initial Assessment is serving to catalyze the thinking of a president  who is keenly aware of the historical perils of a protracted, faraway war  about what he can realistically accomplish in this conflict, and whether his vision for the war and a commitment of American troops is the same as his generals.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama faces a deteriorating security situation in Afghanistan, growing opposition to the war at home from Democrats and a desire to put off any major troop decision while he still needs much political capital to pass major health care legislation in Congress.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But even as
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/09/21/world/asia/21prexy.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  the president expresses skepticism about sending more American troops
 &lt;/a&gt;
 to Afghanistan until he has settled on the right strategy, he is also grappling with a stark reality: it will be very hard to say no to General McChrystal.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama has called Afghanistan a war of necessity, and in the most basic terms he has the same goal as President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot;&gt;
  George W. Bush
 &lt;/a&gt;
 did after the Sept. 11 attacks, to prevent another major terrorist assault.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Whatever decisions I make are going to be based first on a strategy to keep us safe, then well figure out how to resource it,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.cbsnews.com/sections/ftn/main3460.shtml&quot; title=&quot;Transcript&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; interview=&quot;interview&quot; on=&quot;on&quot; face=&quot;Face&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; nations=&quot;Nations&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
  Mr. Obama said Sunday on CBSs Face the Nation
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Were not going to put the cart before the horse and just think by sending more troops were automatically going to make Americans safe, he said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The White House expects General McChrystals request to be not just for American troops but for NATO forces as well. This week, the White House is sending questions about his review back to the general in Kabul, Afghanistan, and expects to get responses by the end of next week.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/l/carl_levin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; carl=&quot;Carl&quot; levin.=&quot;Levin.&quot;&gt;
  Carl Levin
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , a Michigan Democrat who heads the Armed Services Committee, said in an interview Monday that he wants to know how the uncertainty surrounding the recent Afghan elections and a plan to reintegrate
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 fighters into Afghan society could affect General McChrystals troop request.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama has had only one meeting so far on the McChrystal review, but aides plan to schedule three or four more after he returns from the Group of 20 summit meeting in Pittsburgh at the end of this week.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Aides said it should take weeks, not months, to make a decision. The presidents been very clear in our discussion that hes open-minded and hes not going to be swayed by political correctness one way or the other, Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/j/james_l_jones/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; james=&quot;James&quot; l.=&quot;L.&quot; jones.=&quot;Jones.&quot;&gt;
  James L. Jones
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the national security adviser, said in an interview. Different people are going to have different opinions, and he wants to hear them, but at the end of the day, hes going to do what he thinks is the right thing for the United States and most especially for the men and women who have to respond to his orders.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senior officers who work with General McChrystal say he was surprised by the dire condition of the Afghan mission when he assumed command in June.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 His concerns went beyond the strength and resilience of the insurgency. General McChrystal was surprised by the lack of efficient military organization at the NATO headquarters and that a significant percentage of the troops were not positioned to carry out effective counterinsurgency operations.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 There was a sense among General McChrystals staff that the military effort in Afghanistan was disjointed and had not learned from the lessons of the past years of the war.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 We havent been fighting in Afghanistan for eight years, said one officer. Weve been fighting in Afghanistan for one year, eight times in a row.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In his assessment, General McChrystal also portrayed a more sophisticated Taliban foe that uses propaganda effectively and taps into the Afghan prison system as a training ground.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Taliban leaders based in Pakistan appoint shadow governors for most provinces, install their own courts, levy taxes, conscript fighters and wield savvy propagandists. They stand in sharp contrast to a corrupt and inept government.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 And Taliban fighters exert control not only through bombs and bullets. The insurgents wage a silent war of fear, intimidation and persuasion throughout the year  not just during the warmer weather fighting season  to gain control over the population, the general said in his report.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Administration officials said that the generals assessment, while very important, was just one component in the presidents thinking.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.cnn.com/video/#/video/politics/2009/09/20/king.obama.interview.cnn?iref=videosearch&quot; title=&quot;Video&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; interview=&quot;interview&quot; on=&quot;on&quot; cnns=&quot;CNNs&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
  Asked on CNN on Sunday
 &lt;/a&gt;
 why after eight months in office he was still searching for a strategy, Mr. Obama took issue. We put a strategy in place, clarified our goals, but what the election has shown, as well as changing circumstances in Pakistan, is that this is going to be a very difficult operation, he said, referring to the Afghan election. Weve got to make sure that were constantly refining it to keep our focus on what our primary goals are.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Peter Baker and Thom Shanker contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/nyt_author_id&gt;

<node id="n7480">
<data key="x">0.969502407705</data>
<data key="y">0.8</data>
<data key="label">Plan to Boost Afghan Forces Splits Obama Advisers</data>
<data key="date">2009-09-27</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  As
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 weighs sending more troops to Afghanistan, one of the most consequential decisions of his presidency, he has discovered that the military is not monolithic in support of the plan and that some of the civilian advisers he respects most have deep reservations.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sectionPromo&quot;&gt;
   &lt;!--at war promo --&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;h5&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/atwar/atwar190.gif&quot; alt=&quot;At&quot; war=&quot;War&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h5&gt;
    &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
     Notes from Afghanistan, Pakistan, Iraq and other areas of conflict in the post-9/11 era.
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      Go to the Blog
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/p&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sidebarArticles&quot;&gt;
   &lt;h4&gt;
    Related
   &lt;/h4&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    Times Topics:
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html&quot;&gt;
     Afghanistan
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/09/27/world/27military.inline.190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;422&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    From top, Senator Jack Reed, former Secretary of State Colin L. Powell and Senator John F. Kerry have expressed degrees of doubt about the prospect of adding to forces in Afghanistan.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s troop request, which was submitted to the Pentagon on Friday,  has reignited a longstanding debate within the military about the virtues of the counterinsurgency strategy popularized by Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot;&gt;
  David H. Petraeus
 &lt;/a&gt;
 in Iraq and now embraced by General McChrystal, the top American and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 commander in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 General McChrystal is expected to ask for as many as 40,000 additional troops for the eight-year-old war, a number that has generated concern among top officers like Gen. George W. Casey Jr., the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/us_army/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; u.s.=&quot;U.S.&quot; army.=&quot;Army.&quot;&gt;
  Army
 &lt;/a&gt;
 chief of staff, who worry about the capacity to provide more soldiers at a time of stress on the force, officials said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The competing advice and concerns fuel a pivotal struggle to shape the presidents thinking about a war that he inherited but may come to define his tenure. Among the most important outside voices has been that of former Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/colin_l_powell/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; colin=&quot;Colin&quot; l.=&quot;L.&quot; powell.=&quot;Powell.&quot;&gt;
  Colin L. Powell
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , a retired four-star Army general, who visited Mr. Obama in the Oval Office this month and expressed skepticism that more troops would guarantee success. According to people briefed on the discussion, Mr. Powell reminded the president of his longstanding view that military missions should be clearly defined.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Powell is one of the three people outside the administration, along with Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/k/john_kerry/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; kerry.=&quot;Kerry.&quot;&gt;
  John F. Kerry
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/r/jack_reed/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; jack=&quot;Jack&quot; reed.=&quot;Reed.&quot;&gt;
  Jack Reed
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , considered by White House aides to be  most influential in this current debate. All have  expressed varying degrees of doubt about the wisdom of sending more forces to Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Kerry, Democrat of Massachusetts and chairman of the Foreign Relations Committee, has warned of repeating the mistakes of Vietnam, where he served, and has floated the idea of a more limited counterterrorist mission. Mr. Reed, Democrat of Rhode Island and an Army veteran, has not ruled out supporting more troops but said the burden of proof was on commanders to justify it.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In the West Wing, beyond Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , who has advocated an alternative strategy to the troop buildup, other presidential advisers sound dubious about more troops, including
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/e/rahm_emanuel/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; rahm=&quot;Rahm&quot; emanuel.=&quot;Emanuel.&quot;&gt;
  Rahm Emanuel
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the chief of staff, and Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/j/james_l_jones/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; james=&quot;James&quot; l.=&quot;L.&quot; jones.=&quot;Jones.&quot;&gt;
  James L. Jones
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the national security adviser, according to people who have spoken with them. At the same time, Mr. Obama is also hearing from more hawkish figures, including Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/h/richard_c_holbrooke/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; richard=&quot;Richard&quot; c.=&quot;C.&quot; holbrooke.=&quot;Holbrooke.&quot;&gt;
  Richard Holbrooke
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the special representative for Afghanistan and Pakistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 General McChrystals troop request, which has not been made public, was given to Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , by the general in a meeting in Germany on Friday. Admiral Mullen arrived back in Washington on Friday night with one paper copy for himself and one for Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr.  Gates has not endorsed General McChrystals request yet, viewing the situation as complicated, said one person who has spoken with him. But Mr. Gates, who will be an influential voice in Mr. Obamas decision, has also left open the door for more troops and warned of the consequences of failure in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Although Mr. Obama has called Afghanistan a war of necessity, he has left members of both parties uncertain about the degree of his commitment to a large and sustained military presence. Even some advisers said they thought Mr. Obamas support for the war as a senator and presidential candidate was at least partly a way of contrasting it with what he saw as a reckless war in Iraq.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 His decision to send 21,000 more troops to Afghanistan early this year, which will bring the number of American troops there to 68,000 this fall, was made hurriedly within weeks of coming into office to stanch the tactical erosion on the ground and provide security during Afghan elections.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But with those elections now marred by
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2009/09/21/world/asia/0921-afghan-election-analysis.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; graphic=&quot;graphic&quot;&gt;
  fraud allegations
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the latest troop request is forcing Mr. Obama to decide whether he wants to fully engage in Afghanistan for the rest of his term or make a drastic change of course. Some advisers said the varying views reflected the complicated nature of a debate. The troop request follows the strategy unveiled by Mr. Obama in March to focus more on protecting the Afghan population, building infrastructure and improving governance, rather than just hunting the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 . On Friday, a
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/u/united_nations/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; united=&quot;United&quot; nations.=&quot;Nations.&quot;&gt;
  United Nations
 &lt;/a&gt;
 report said that from January to August, 1,500 civilians were killed, about two-thirds of them by militants.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Admiral Mullen has endorsed the idea of more troops and will be at the table representing the military. General McChrystal and ambassadors from the region will get a chance to participate in  meetings with the president through a secure video hookup.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Other officers, who have served in Iraq and Afghanistan and say they admire General McChrystal nonetheless, have privately expressed doubt that additional troops will make a difference. Others question the broader impact of such a buildup on the overall armed forces.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 If a request for more forces comes to the Army, well have to assess what that will do in terms of stress on the force, said an  Army official, who asked not to be identified because  General McChrystals troop request had not been made  public.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 General Casey, whose institutional role as Army chief is to protect his force, has a goal  to increase by 2012 a soldiers time at home, to two years at home for every year served, from the current one year for every year of duty in Iraq or Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Advisers who have Mr. Obamas ear have raised other questions. Mr. Powell spoke with Mr. Obama about a variety of topics, but his remarks on Afghanistan resonated in the White House. The question the president has to answer is, What will more troops do? Mr. Powell told reporters before a speech in California last week. You have to not just add troops. You need a clear definition of your mission and then you can determine whether you need more troops or other resources.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In an interview, Senator Kerry, who met with Admiral Mullen last week, said that he had not made up his mind about the troop buildup, but that in Vietnam, the underlying assumptions were flawed, and the number of troops werent going to make a difference.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator Reed, who met with Mr. Biden, was more measured, but said the president needed to look at the capacity of Afghan forces and the prospects of reconciliation with moderate Taliban members. You want to make sure you have the best operational plan to carry out the strategy, he said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;
&lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n7788">
<data key="x">1.15890850722</data>
<data key="y">0.8</data>
<data key="label">Obama Rules Out Large Reduction in Afghan Force</data>
<data key="date">2009-10-07</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 told Congressional leaders on Tuesday that he would not substantially reduce American forces in Afghanistan or shift the mission to just hunting terrorists there, but he indicated that he remained undecided about the major troop buildup proposed by his commanding general.
&lt;/p&gt;

   &lt;h2&gt;
    Times Topics:
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html&quot;&gt;
     Afghanistan
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--Article Comments Include--&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/10/07/world/07prexy.inline.190.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;150&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    Luke Sharrett/The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    Three Republicans, from left, Representative John Boehner and Senators John McCain and Mitch McConnell on Tuesday.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Meeting with leaders from both parties at the White House, Mr. Obama seemed to be searching for some sort of middle ground, saying he wanted to dispense with the straw man argument that this is about either doubling down or leaving Afghanistan, as White House officials later described his remarks.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But as the war approached its eight-year anniversary on Wednesday, the session underscored the perilous crosscurrents awaiting Mr. Obama. While some Democrats said they would support whatever he decided, others challenged him about sending more troops. And Republicans pressed him to order the escalation without delay, leading to a pointed exchange between the president and Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/john_mccain/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; mccain.=&quot;McCain.&quot;&gt;
  John McCain
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of Arizona, his Republican opponent from last years election.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. McCain told the president that time is not on our side. He added, This should not be a leisurely process, according to several people in the room.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A few minutes later, Mr. Obama replied, John, I can assure you this wont be leisurely, according to several attendees. No one feels more urgency to get this right than I do.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Still, compared with the harsh debate over health care, the tone was civil and restrained during the 75-minute meeting in the State Dining Room as Mr. Obama, Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and about 30 members of Congress gathered around a large table with only glasses of water and notebooks in front of them.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama summoned the lawmakers to assure them that he would keep their concerns in mind as he considered the request of his commander in Afghanistan, Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , for as many as 40,000 more troops. The president plans to meet with his national security team on Wednesday to talk about Pakistan and on Friday to talk about Afghanistan. Aides plan to schedule one more meeting before he decides on General McChrystals proposal.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Several administration officials and lawmakers who attended the session on Tuesday said Mr. Obama was intent on using it to dismiss any impression that he would consider pulling out of Afghanistan. There is no option that would entail a dramatic reduction in troops, said one administration official, who, like others quoted in this article, requested anonymity to discuss the closed-door meeting.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama and Mr. Biden made it clear that
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  the option Mr. Biden had proposed
 &lt;/a&gt;
 was not a pure counterterrorism alternative, relying only on drones and Special Forces to track down leaders of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 . Instead, Mr. Bidens approach would increase the use of such surgical strikes while leaving the overall size of the American force in Afghanistan roughly at the 68,000 troops currently authorized.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 And in the final moments of the meeting, Mr. Obama sought to put to rest suspicions of friction with General McChrystal. Im the one who hired him, Mr. Obama said, according to participants. I put him there to give me a frank assessment.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A joint appearance afterward on the White House driveway by the two top Democratic Congressional leaders demonstrated Mr. Obamas political challenge. The one thing that I thought was interesting was that everyone, Democrats and Republicans, said whatever decision you make, well support it basically, said Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/r/harry_reid/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; harry=&quot;Harry&quot; reid.=&quot;Reid.&quot;&gt;
  Harry Reid
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the majority leader.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/nancy_pelosi/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nancy=&quot;Nancy&quot; pelosi.=&quot;Pelosi.&quot;&gt;
  Nancy Pelosi
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the House speaker, smiled and raised her eyebrows in apparent disagreement. Whether we agreed with it or voted for it remains to be seen when we see what the president puts forth, she said. But I think there was a real display of universal respect for the manner in which he was approaching it.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 At least three Democrats  Ms. Pelosi; Senator Carl Levin, the Armed Services Committee chairman; and Representative David R. Obey, the Appropriations Committee chairman  voiced reservations during the meeting about increasing troops, according to those in attendance.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 There were a number of people who spoke out with a lot of caution about getting in deeper and what the endpoint is, Mr. Levin said in an interview. Mr. Levin, who promoted accelerated training of Afghan forces, then met alone with Mr. Obama  to expand on his views.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Others shared their skepticism in interviews. Clearly, there is hesitancy about the prospect of sending 40,000 more troops, said Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/l/nita_m_lowey/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nita=&quot;Nita&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; lowey.=&quot;Lowey.&quot;&gt;
  Nita M. Lowey
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Democrat of New York.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/k/john_kerry/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; kerry.=&quot;Kerry.&quot;&gt;
  John Kerry
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , chairman of the Foreign Relations Committee, said after the meeting that it would be irresponsible to send more troops until it became clear what is possible in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Some Democrats were more supportive of General McChrystals request, including Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/f/dianne_feinstein/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; dianne=&quot;Dianne&quot; feinstein.=&quot;Feinstein.&quot;&gt;
  Dianne Feinstein
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , head of the  intelligence committee, and Representative Ike Skelton, head of the  Armed Services Committee.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I said the real war in Afghanistan did not start until March, when the president made the speech on strategy, Mr. Skelton said in an interview, referring to the strategy Mr. Obama put in place shortly after taking office. There was no strategy before that, he said, and so the president ought to give General McChrystal what he needs to execute it.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Republicans pressed even harder. After the meeting, Mr. McCain warned against any middle ground. Half measures is what I worry about, he said. Citing the Bush administrations experience in Iraq, he added that half measures lead to failure over time and an erosion of American public support.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama separately pointed to American successes against Al Qaeda in a series of recent missile strikes and Special Forces raids. During a visit to the National Counterterrorism Center just outside Washington on Tuesday, he said Al Qaeda had lost operational capacity but he vowed to continue pressing the battle to cripple the network around the world.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 White House officials said the presidents visit was not related to the Afghanistan review. But the public focus on efforts to eliminate Al Qaedas top hierarchy through surgical strikes could provide political cover for Mr. Obama should he reject the most expansive request for 40,000 more troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot;&gt;
  David H. Petraeus
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , who oversees operations in Iraq and Afghanistan, told a military conference on Tuesday that the presidents strategy review was progressing toward a decision. It is moving quite rapidly, he told the Association of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/us_army/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; united=&quot;United&quot; states=&quot;States&quot; army.=&quot;Army.&quot;&gt;
  United States Army
 &lt;/a&gt;
 . There is a recognition of the need to move through this.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/10/05/world/05military.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  general said the effort in Afghanistan
 &lt;/a&gt;
 required a sustained, substantial commitment, but he declined to say if that meant more troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Elisabeth Bumiller and Carl Hulse contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;

<data key="label">Obama Meeting Advisers Amid Debate on Afghan Policy</data>
<data key="date">2009-10-07</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  Eight years to the day after the start of the war in Afghanistan, the White House and Congress were agonizing on Wednesday about what to do next in that isolated, mountainous country that has been called the graveyard of empires.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;

     &lt;/a&gt;

      Obama Speaks on Counterterrorism
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h2&gt;
    &lt;div class=&quot;clear&quot;&gt;

    &lt;/a&gt;

   &lt;/h2&gt;

    &lt;/a&gt;
    (October 7, 2009)

   &lt;h2&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/10/07/world/asia/07prexy.html?ref=asia&quot;&gt;
     Obama Rules Out Large Reduction in Afghan Force
    &lt;/a&gt;
    (October 7, 2009)
   &lt;/h2&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    Times Topics:
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html&quot;&gt;
     Afghanistan
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--Article Comments Include--&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A day after telling Congressional leaders that he would not substantially reduce American forces in Afghanistan or shift the mission to just hunting terrorists there,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 was scheduled to confer with his national security team Wednesday afternoon on Afghanistan and Pakistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The session at the White House, which was expected to last at least until early evening,  was one of several official gatherings in the capital on American policy in Afghanistan. So far, President Obama appears to be undecided about how to respond to the proposal by his commanding general for a major troop buildup.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Were at a process of going through this fairly systematically,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_gibbs/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; gibbs.=&quot;Gibbs.&quot;&gt;
  Robert Gibbs
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the presidents chief spokesman, said before the White House discussion.  Emphasizing that the talk would go well beyond troop levels, Mr. Gibbs said, I think everybody is waiting for people to walk out of a room and give everybody a number.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Gibbs said the president had received a formal request for troops from the commander in Afghanistan, Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 . He declined to discuss specifics of the request.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Earlier Wednesday, Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 met with Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 at the vice presidents residence at the Naval Observatory in Washington. Then Mr. Gates went to the White House, where he conferred with Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/j/james_l_jones/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; james=&quot;James&quot; l.=&quot;L.&quot; jones.=&quot;Jones.&quot;&gt;
  James L. Jones
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the presidents national security adviser.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 On Capitol Hill, the Senate Foreign Relations Committee was scheduled to hear from a panel of experts on Wednesday afternoon on the threat from
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 in Afghanistan and beyond.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 There have also been scattered antiwar protests in Washington timed for the anniversary, although none as large or emotional as those of the Vietnam era.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 For the moment, President Obama seemed to be searching for some sort of middle ground, saying he wanted to dispense with the straw man argument that this is about either doubling down or leaving Afghanistan, as White House officials described his remarks on Tuesday during a meeting with leaders from both parties.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The meeting on Tuesday and the series of Afghanistan-related events on Wednesday underscored the perilous crosscurrents awaiting Mr. Obama. While some Democrats said on Tuesday that they would support whatever he decided to do, others challenged him about sending more troops. And Republicans pressed him to order the escalation without delay, leading to a pointed exchange between the president and Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/john_mccain/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; mccain.=&quot;McCain.&quot;&gt;
  John McCain
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of Arizona, his Republican opponent from last years election.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. McCain told the president that time is not on our side. He added, This should not be a leisurely process, according to several people in the room.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A few minutes later, Mr. Obama replied, John, I can assure you this wont be leisurely, according to several attendees. No one feels more urgency to get this right than I do.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Still, compared with the harsh debate over health care, the tone was civil and restrained during the 75-minute meeting in the State Dining Room as Mr. Obama, Vice President Biden and about 30 members of Congress gathered around a large table with only glasses of water and notebooks in front of them.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama had summoned the lawmakers to assure them that he would keep their concerns in mind as he considered the request of General McChrystal for as many as 40,000 more troops. Several administration officials and lawmakers who attended the session on Tuesday said Mr. Obama was intent on using it to dismiss any impression that he would consider pulling out of Afghanistan. There is no option that would entail a dramatic reduction in troops, said one administration official, who, like others quoted in this article, requested anonymity to discuss the closed-door meeting.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama and Mr. Biden made it clear that the option Mr. Biden had proposed was not a pure counterterrorism alternative, relying only on drones and Special Forces to track down leaders of Al Qaeda. Instead, Mr. Bidens approach would increase the use of such surgical strikes while leaving the overall size of the American force in Afghanistan roughly at the 68,000 troops currently authorized.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 And in the final moments of the meeting, Mr. Obama sought to put to rest suspicions of friction with General McChrystal. Im the one who hired him, Mr. Obama said, according to participants. I put him there to give me a frank assessment.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A joint appearance afterward on the White House driveway by the two top Democratic Congressional leaders demonstrated Mr. Obamas political challenge. The one thing that I thought was interesting was that everyone, Democrats and Republicans, said whatever decision you make, well support it basically, said Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/r/harry_reid/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; harry=&quot;Harry&quot; reid.=&quot;Reid.&quot;&gt;
  Harry Reid
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the majority leader.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/nancy_pelosi/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nancy=&quot;Nancy&quot; pelosi.=&quot;Pelosi.&quot;&gt;
  Nancy Pelosi
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the House speaker, smiled and raised her eyebrows in apparent disagreement. Whether we agreed with it or voted for it remains to be seen when we see what the president puts forth, she said. But I think there was a real display of universal respect for the manner in which he was approaching it.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 At least three Democrats  Ms. Pelosi; Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/l/carl_levin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; carl=&quot;Carl&quot; levin.=&quot;Levin.&quot;&gt;
  Carl Levin
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the Armed Services Committee chairman; and Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/david_r_obey/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; obey.=&quot;Obey.&quot;&gt;
  David R. Obey
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the Appropriations Committee chairman  voiced reservations during the meeting about increasing troops, according to those in attendance.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 There were a number of people who spoke out with a lot of caution about getting in deeper and what the endpoint is, Mr. Levin said in an interview. Mr. Levin, who promoted accelerated training of Afghan forces, then met alone with Mr. Obama to expand on his views.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Others shared their skepticism in interviews. Clearly, there is hesitancy about the prospect of sending 40,000 more troops, said Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/l/nita_m_lowey/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nita=&quot;Nita&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; lowey.=&quot;Lowey.&quot;&gt;
  Nita M. Lowey
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Democrat of New York.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/k/john_kerry/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; kerry.=&quot;Kerry.&quot;&gt;
  John Kerry
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , chairman of the Foreign Relations Committee, said after the meeting that it would be irresponsible to send more troops until it became clear what is possible in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Some Democrats were more supportive of General McChrystals request, including Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/f/dianne_feinstein/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; dianne=&quot;Dianne&quot; feinstein.=&quot;Feinstein.&quot;&gt;
  Dianne Feinstein
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , head of the intelligence committee, and Representative Ike Skelton, head of the Armed Services Committee.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 I said the real war in Afghanistan did not start until March, when the president made the speech on strategy, Mr. Skelton said in an interview, referring to the strategy Mr. Obama put in place shortly after taking office. There was no strategy before that, he said, and so the president ought to give General McChrystal what he needs to execute it.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Republicans pressed even harder. After the meeting, Mr. McCain warned against any middle ground. Half measures is what I worry about, he said. Citing the Bush administrations experience in Iraq, he added that half measures lead to failure over time and an erosion of American public support.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama separately pointed to American successes against Al Qaeda in a series of recent missile strikes and Special Forces raids. During a visit to the National Counterterrorism Center just outside Washington on Tuesday, he said Al Qaeda had lost operational capacity but he vowed to continue pressing the battle to cripple the network around the world.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 White House officials said the presidents visit was not related to the Afghanistan review. But the public focus on efforts to eliminate Al Qaedas top hierarchy through surgical strikes could provide political cover for Mr. Obama should he reject the most expansive request for 40,000 more troops. (The American campaign in Afghanistan began on Oct. 7, 2001, with raids by United States and British planes against suspected sanctuaries of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/osama_bin_laden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; osama=&quot;Osama&quot; bin=&quot;bin&quot; laden.=&quot;Laden.&quot;&gt;
  Osama bin Laden
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s followers.)
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot;&gt;
  David H. Petraeus
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , who oversees operations in Iraq and Afghanistan, told a military conference on Tuesday that the presidents strategy review was progressing toward a decision. It is moving quite rapidly, he told the Association of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/us_army/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; united=&quot;United&quot; states=&quot;States&quot; army.=&quot;Army.&quot;&gt;
  United States Army
 &lt;/a&gt;
 . There is a recognition of the need to move through this.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The general said the effort in Afghanistan required a sustained, substantial commitment, but he declined to say if that meant more troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Elisabeth Bumiller, Carl Hulse and David Stout contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
