&lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n8675">
<data key="x">1.25361155698</data>
<data key="y">0.8</data>
<data key="label">All Afghan War Options by Obama Aides Said to Call for More Troops</data>
<data key="date">2009-11-08</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  Advisers to
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 are preparing three options for escalating the war effort in Afghanistan, all of them calling for more American troops, as he moves closer to a decision on the way forward in the eight-year-old war, officials said Saturday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The options include Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s request for roughly another 40,000 troops; a middle scenario sending about 30,000 more troops; and a lower alternative involving 20,000 to 25,000 reinforcements, according to the officials, who insisted on anonymity to discuss internal deliberations. Officials hope to present the options to Mr. Obama this week before he leaves on a trip to Asia.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 While some civilian and military officials believe Mr. Obama is seeking a middle ground in the debate over Afghanistan, aides denied he has made any decision or is leaning toward any of the options. Still, Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 appears to be supportive of the middle option, some officials said, and his view is thought to be pivotal because of Mr. Obamas respect for him and his status as a holdover from a Republican administration.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The three options define the contours of a debate that has played out in public for more than two months. General McChrystal, the top American and allied commander in Afghanistan, and his advocates argue the war cannot be won without a major infusion of forces to protect the population and ultimately turn it against the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 . Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and others oppose a buildup in a war they believe cannot be won through conventional means and that diverts attention from Pakistan, where
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 is primarily located. There are currently 68,000 American troops in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The range of alternatives under discussion suggests that the president has rejected the extremes on either end. He appears inclined to send more troops  with the only question being how many  and seems not to be seriously considering General McChrystals highest proposal of 80,000 more troops.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Still, any of the options on the table would generate opposition on either the political left or right. If he approves anything less than General McChrystals 40,000-troop option, Mr. Obama could face criticism from Republicans and some moderate Democrats, while any troop increase would provoke anger among liberals and others who have increasingly soured on the war.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 McClatchy Newspapers
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.mcclatchydc.com/227/story/78516.html&quot; title=&quot;The&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  reported
 &lt;/a&gt;
 Saturday that Mr. Obama is nearing a decision to approve the middle option being drawn up by advisers, citing unnamed administration and military officials. White House officials denied Mr. Obama has made a decision or favors any of the options at this point, noting that they have not been formally presented to him. But administration officials confirmed that the 30,000-troop plan is under consideration.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 If he were to go with that, Mr. Obama could try to make up the difference in what General McChrystal wants by pressing
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 allies to do more. Britain has already agreed to send another 500 troops, and four senior American officials flew to Brussels last week to brief representatives of other nations that have forces in Afghanistan, to solicit their views and build support for more help.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 There could be variations within each of the three options as well that could increase or decrease the number of troops needed, officials said. Troop levels would hinge, for instance, on the administrations assessment of how many former Taliban fighters can be peacefully reintegrated into Afghan society and to what extent improved governance at various levels could prevent disaffected Afghans from siding with insurgents.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Officials are focusing on an approach predicated on the belief that the Taliban cannot be entirely eradicated in Afghanistan and that Al Qaeda is the real threat to American interests. The main goal for American forces, then, would be to protect the 10 most important population centers in Afghanistan and keep the Taliban isolated long enough to train Afghan security forces to take over the fight.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama has met with his national security advisers seven times since General McChrystal sent his assessment Aug. 31. Officials hope to schedule another meeting this week.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The presidents departure for Asia was delayed a day until Thursday so that he can fly to
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/f/fort_hood_texas/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; fort=&quot;Fort&quot; hood=&quot;Hood&quot; army=&quot;Army&quot; base.=&quot;base.&quot;&gt;
  Fort Hood
 &lt;/a&gt;
 on Tuesday for a service commemorating the victims of last weeks mass shooting.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Elisabeth Bumiller and Eric Schmitt contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/nyt_author_id&gt;

<data key="x">1.34831460674</data>
<data key="y">0.5</data>
<data key="label">Top Obama Advisers Favor Adding Troops in Afghanistan</data>
<data key="date">2009-11-11</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , and Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 are coalescing around a proposal to send 30,000 or more additional American troops to
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; afghanistan.=&quot;Afghanistan.&quot;&gt;
  Afghanistan
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , but
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 remains unsatisfied with answers he has gotten about how vigorously the governments of Afghanistan and
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/pakistan/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; pakistan.=&quot;Pakistan.&quot;&gt;
  Pakistan
 &lt;/a&gt;
 would help execute a new strategy, administration officials said Tuesday.
&lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html&quot;&gt;
     Afghanistan
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;

    The Taliban blew up an American-financed health clinic, above, in Kunar Province, Afghanistan.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama is to consider four final options in a meeting with his national security team on Wednesday, his press secretary,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_gibbs/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; gibbs.=&quot;Gibbs.&quot;&gt;
  Robert Gibbs
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , told reporters. The options outline different troop levels, other officials said, but they also assume different goals  including how much of Afghanistan the troops would seek to control  and different time frames and expectations for the training of Afghan security forces.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Three of the options call for specific levels of additional troops. The low-end option would add 20,000 to 25,000 troops, a middle option calls for about 30,000, and another embraces Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s request for roughly 40,000 more troops. Administration officials said that a fourth option was added only in the past few days. They declined to identify any troop level attached to it.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Gates, a Republican who served as President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot;&gt;
  George W. Bush
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s last defense secretary, and who commands considerable respect from the president, is expected to be pivotal in Mr. Obamas decision. But administration officials cautioned that Mr. Obama had not yet made up his mind, and that other top advisers, among them Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and the White House chief of staff,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/e/rahm_emanuel/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; rahm=&quot;Rahm&quot; emanuel.=&quot;Emanuel.&quot;&gt;
  Rahm Emanuel
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , remained skeptical of the value of a buildup.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In the Situation Room meetings and other sessions, some officials have expressed deep reservations about President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/k/hamid_karzai/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hamid=&quot;Hamid&quot; karzai.=&quot;Karzai.&quot;&gt;
  Hamid Karzai
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , who emerged the victor of a disputed Afghan election. They said there was no evidence that Mr. Karzai would carry through on promises to crack down on corruption or the drug trade or that his government was capable of training enough reliable Afghan troops and police officers for Mr. Obama to describe a credible exit strategy.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Officials said that although the president had no doubt about what large numbers of United States troops could achieve on their own in Afghanistan, he repeatedly asked questions during recent meetings on Afghanistan about whether a sizable American force might undercut the urgency of the preparations of the Afghan forces who are learning to stand up on their own.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Hes simply not convinced yet that you can do a lasting counterinsurgency strategy if there is no one to hand it off to, one participant said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama, officials said, has expressed similar concerns about Pakistans willingness to attack
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 leaders who are operating out of the Pakistani city of Quetta and commanding forces that are mounting attacks across the border in Afghanistan. While Pakistan has mounted military operations against some Taliban groups in recent weeks, one official noted, its been focused on the Taliban who are targeting the Pakistani government, but not those who are running operations in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama himself seems to be hedging his bets, particularly on the performance of Mr. Karzai, who is considered by American officials to be an unreliable partner and is now widely derided in the White House. Mr. Obama told ABC News during an interview on Monday that given the weakness of the Karzai government in Kabul, his administration was seeking provincial government actors that have legitimacy in the right now.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Officials said that while Admiral Mullen and Mrs. Clinton were generally in sync with Mr. Gates in supporting an option of about 30,000 troops, there were variations in their positions and they were not working in lock step. Admiral Mullens spokesman, Capt. John Kirby, said that the admiral was providing his advice to the president in private and would not comment. Geoff Morrell, the Pentagon press secretary, would not comment on Mr. Gatess position.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 A focus of Mr. Obamas meeting on Wednesday with his national security advisers, officials said, will be to discuss some of their differences as well as those of the presidents other advisers. Officials also said there was a possibility that Mr. Obama might choose to phase in additional troops over time, with a schedule that depended on the timing of the arrival of any additional
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 troops and on how soon Afghan security forces would be able to do more on their own.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Officials said that no decision was expected from Mr. Obama on Wednesday, but that he would mull over the discussions at the meeting during a trip to Asia that begins Thursday. Mr. Obama is not due back in Washington until next Thursday.  Officials said that it was possible that he could announce his decision in the three days before Thanksgiving, which is on Nov. 26, but that an announcement in the first week of December seemed more likely.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Should Mr. Obama choose to send about 30,000 troops, a military official said, brigades would most likely be sent from the 101st Airborne Division at Fort Campbell, Ky., and the 10th Mountain Division at Fort Drum, N.Y. In addition, 4,000 troops would be sent as trainers for the Afghan security forces, the military official said. A brigade is about 3,500 to 5,000 soldiers.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/r/jack_reed/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; jack=&quot;Jack&quot; reed.=&quot;Reed.&quot;&gt;
  Jack Reed
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the Rhode Island Democrat who has been an influential adviser in the Afghanistan debate, said that one of the most difficult issues was determining the effects of a large American troop presence on the country.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Its more about, hey, are we creating such a large footprint that its easier for the Afghans to walk way from their responsibility? Mr. Reed said. I dont think thats one that can be resolved. Youre making a judgment about that one, and not one you can solve with arithmetic.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Peter Baker, Eric Schmitt and Mark Landler contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/nyt_author_id&gt;

<data key="x">1.4430176565</data>
<data key="y">0.5</data>
<data key="label">Obama May Add 30,000 Troops in Afghanistan</data>
<data key="date">2009-11-25</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 said Tuesday that he was determined to finish the job in Afghanistan, and his aides signaled to allies that he would send as many as 25,000 to 30,000 additional American troops there even as they cautioned that the final number remained in flux.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;leftNavTabs&quot;&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;

   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sectionPromo&quot;&gt;
   &lt;!--at war promo --&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;h5&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/atwar/atwar190.gif&quot; alt=&quot;At&quot; war=&quot;War&quot; /&gt;

   &lt;/h4&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/11/25/world/asia/25rollout.html?ref=politics&quot;&gt;
     News Analysis: U.S. Strategy on Afghanistan Will Contain Many Messages
    &lt;/a&gt;
    (November 25, 2009)
   &lt;/h2&gt;
   &lt;h2&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/11/25/world/asia/25briefs-Afghanistan.html?ref=politics&quot;&gt;
     World Briefing | Asia: Afghanistan: 15 in Corruption Inquiry
    &lt;/a&gt;
    (November 25, 2009)
   &lt;/h2&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;promo&quot;&gt;
   Blog
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;

   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;h5&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     The Caucus
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h5&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;

    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     Join the discussion.
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;ul class=&quot;refer&quot; style=&quot;font-size:75%&quot;&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/pages/politics/index.html&quot;&gt;
     More Politics News
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
  &lt;/ul&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;singleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--Article Comments Include--&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The White House said Mr. Obama had completed his consultations with his war council on Monday night and would formally announce his decision in a national address in the next week, probably on Tuesday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 At a news conference in the East Room with Prime Minister
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/s/manmohan_singh/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; manmohan=&quot;Manmohan&quot; singh.=&quot;Singh.&quot;&gt;
  Manmohan Singh
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of India, Mr. Obama suggested that his approach would break from the policies he had inherited from the Bush administration and said that the goals would be to keep
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 from using the region to launch more attacks against the United States and to bring more stability to
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/afghanistan/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; afghanistan.=&quot;Afghanistan.&quot;&gt;
  Afghanistan
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 After eight years  some of those years in which we did not have, I think, either the resources or the strategy to get the job done  it is my intention to finish the job, he said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He said that he would outline his Afghanistan strategy after Thanksgiving, adding, I feel very confident that when the American people hear a clear rationale for what were doing there and how we intend to achieve our goals, that they will be supportive.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Though he and his advisers have drawn up benchmarks to measure progress and put pressure on the Afghan government to do its part, Mr. Obama offered no details in his public remarks on Tuesday. He was also silent on precisely what would constitute finishing the job in Afghanistan or how soon he envisioned being able to begin extricating the United States from the war there.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 While the troop levels he orders will go a long way toward defining his position, the White House has stressed that Mr. Obamas review has gone far beyond the numbers to better define the military and civilian-aid components of the effort in Afghanistan, how they fit into efforts to combat Al Qaeda in Pakistan and how to ensure that the American commitment in the region is not open-ended.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 At the meeting on Monday night, Mr. Obama went around the table in the White House Situation Room asking his senior advisers for summations of their individual assessments and to voice any concerns they still had, said an administration official who was briefed on the two-hour meeting.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 There was a lot of back and forth, said the official, with Mr. Obama interjecting questions and top aides cutting each other off at times. When the  meeting finished shortly after 10 p.m., some of the senior advisers lingered in small groups to continue their discussions, said the official, who like others interviewed for this article spoke on the condition of anonymity because of the meetings confidentiality.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The meeting covered a wide variety of issues, including benchmarks to measure progress by Pakistan and Afghanistan, as well as the specific number of additional American troops to send.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Although his aides told some allies that the troop increase would most likely be slightly below 30,000  there are currently 68,000 American troops in Afghanistan  several officials said Mr. Obama did not appear completely settled on a final number.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Hes still not happy, one official said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 One reason for Mr. Obamas disquiet might be discontent among the members of his own party on Capitol Hill over the prospect of escalating the war and paying for it. Among those present at Monday nights session was
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/peter_orszag/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; peter=&quot;Peter&quot; orszag.=&quot;Orszag.&quot;&gt;
  Peter R. Orszag
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the White House budget director.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Before a meeting with Mr. Obama on Tuesday afternoon,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/nancy_pelosi/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nancy=&quot;Nancy&quot; pelosi.=&quot;Pelosi.&quot;&gt;
  Nancy Pelosi
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the House speaker, said during a conference call of economists and bloggers that there was
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/11/24/world/asia/24policy.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  serious unrest in our caucus
 &lt;/a&gt;
 about can we afford this war.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Ms. Pelosi said she did not want to sacrifice the partys domestic agenda to the cost of the troop buildup. The American people believe that if something is in our national security interest, we have to be able to afford it, she said. That doesnt mean that we hold everything else hostage to that.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Administration officials said that during the Monday meeting, officials discussed a proposal to deploy the American troops in waves, the first of which would go early next year to be in place in southern or eastern Afghanistan by spring. They said the American military should be able to deploy one brigade per quarter.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 One administration official involved in Afghanistan policy said the president and his top advisers were thinking in terms of exit strategies and not necessarily exit timetables. He compared the current thinking to the conditional engagement that President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot;&gt;
  George W. Bush
 &lt;/a&gt;
 used in Iraq.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 As Afghan security forces are trained and deployed, the official said, American officials and commanders would watch closely to determine when operational control of a given area could be turned over to them. That is what happened in Iraq, as American forces gradually turned over control of territory to Iraqis once they had proved their ability.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 As you go along, you might have some target dates, the administration official said, noting as an example the proposal by Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/l/carl_levin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; carl=&quot;Carl&quot; levin.=&quot;Levin.&quot;&gt;
  Carl Levin
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the Michigan Democrat who leads the Armed Services Committee, that by 2012, the Afghan Army should be increased to 240,000 soldiers from 92,000, and police forces to 160,000 officers from 84,000.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Obama declined to say what day he would make his announcement, but officials said the Congressional leadership had been invited to the White House for a briefing next Tuesday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Administration officials said that as part of his Afghanistan strategy, Mr. Obama would also announce
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/11/20/world/asia/20policy.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  strict benchmarks
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , or performance targets, which the United States will expect the Afghan government to meet. Mr. Obama will be tying both military and economic aid to Afghanistan to those targets, the officials said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 As the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/11/23/world/asia/23military.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  debate over the size of the troop increase
 &lt;/a&gt;
 has played out over the last few months, an increase of about 30,000 reinforcements has won the support of Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 That number would fall between the 40,000 additional troops requested by the American commander in Afghanistan, Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , and the far smaller number favored by some Obama advisers, including Vice President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot;&gt;
  Joseph R. Biden Jr.
 &lt;/a&gt;
 Mr. Obama will also be making a broader appeal for Afghanistans neighbors and regional actors to play a role, the officials said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 We have to do it as part of a broader international community, Mr. Obama said at the news conference. So one of the things Im going to be discussing is the obligations of our international partners in this process.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 After Mr. Obama announces his Afghanistan strategy, Mrs. Clinton will brief
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 allies at a meeting of foreign ministers in Brussels on Dec. 3 and 4. There, Mrs. Clinton is expected to solicit specific contributions from them, including as many as 10,000 additional soldiers, bringing the total number of allied troops in line with General McChrystals request. Administration officials cautioned that they did not expect contributions to be nailed down until January.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Jeff Zeleny, Peter Baker and Mark Landler contributed reporting.
  &lt;/p&gt;

<node id="n9299">
<data key="x">1.53772070626</data>
<data key="y">0.5</data>
<data key="label">Obama Team Defends Policy on Afghanistan</data>
<data key="date">2009-12-03</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  Defense Secretary
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot;&gt;
  Robert M. Gates
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Secretary of State
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/hillary_rodham_clinton/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; hillary=&quot;Hillary&quot; rodham=&quot;Rodham&quot; clinton.=&quot;Clinton.&quot;&gt;
  Hillary Rodham Clinton
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and the nations top military officer on Wednesday laid out a muscular defense of
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 s decision to send 30,000 additional troops to Afghanistan, but they made clear that his plan to begin withdrawing those forces by July 2011 was flexible.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;articleInline&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;leftNavTabs&quot;&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;inlineBox&quot;&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;#secondParagraph&quot; class=&quot;jumpLink&quot;&gt;
   Skip to next paragraph
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;div id=&quot;sectionPromo&quot;&gt;
   &lt;!--at war promo --&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;h5&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/atwar/atwar190.gif&quot; alt=&quot;At&quot; war=&quot;War&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h5&gt;
    &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
     Notes from Afghanistan, Pakistan, Iraq and other areas of conflict in the post-9/11 era.
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
      Go to the Blog
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/p&gt;

   &lt;div class=&quot;singleRule&quot;&gt;

   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;h3 class=&quot;promo&quot;&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/11/30/obamas-surge-strategy-in-afghanistan&quot;&gt;
      Obamas Surge Strategy in Afghanistan
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h3&gt;
    &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/11/30/obamas-surge-strategy-in-afghanistan&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/roomfordebate/roomfordebate75.gif&quot; alt=&quot;Room&quot; for=&quot;for&quot; debate=&quot;Debate&quot; class=&quot;callout&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
     Will 30,000 additional troops be sufficient to curb the insurgency?
    &lt;/p&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://community.nytimes.com/comments/roomfordebate.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/11/30/obamas-surge-strategy-in-afghanistan/&quot; class=&quot;more&quot;&gt;
     &lt;strong&gt;
      Join the Discussion
     &lt;/strong&gt;
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;!--Article Comments Include--&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics7.nytimes.com/images/2009/12/03/world/03policy_CA0/articleInline.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;129&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
    Stephen Crowley/The New York Times
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
    Senators Carl Levin and John McCain questioned President Obama`s foreign policy advisers about Afghanistan on Wednesday.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a name=&quot;secondParagraph&quot;&gt;
&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 At two hearings on Capitol Hill, where they faced deep skepticism about different parts of Mr. Obamas war plan from both parties, they also said that the arrival of the additional forces, while speedy, would not be as fast as Mr. Obama suggested in
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/12/02/world/asia/02prexy.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  a speech to the nation on Tuesday night
 &lt;/a&gt;
 .
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Although most of the additional troops would arrive in Afghanistan in the first six months of next year, as the president announced, Adm.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/michael_g_mullen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; michael=&quot;Michael&quot; g.=&quot;G.&quot; mullen.=&quot;Mullen.&quot;&gt;
  Mike Mullen
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the chairman of the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/j/joint_chiefs_of_staff/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joint=&quot;Joint&quot; chiefs=&quot;Chiefs&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; staff=&quot;Staff&quot;&gt;
  Joint Chiefs of Staff
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , said they would not all be in place until the fall of 2010.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 At the same time, American diplomats said that
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/north_atlantic_treaty_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; north=&quot;North&quot; atlantic=&quot;Atlantic&quot; treaty=&quot;Treaty&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot;&gt;
  NATO
 &lt;/a&gt;
 allies had expressed surprise at Mr. Obamas commitment to begin withdrawing by July 2011.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/h/richard_c_holbrooke/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; richard=&quot;Richard&quot; c.=&quot;C.&quot; holbrooke.=&quot;Holbrooke.&quot;&gt;
  Richard C. Holbrooke
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the administrations special representative for Afghanistan and Pakistan, met Wednesday with officials from several countries to explain the presidents thinking, similar to what Mr. Gates, Mrs. Clinton and Admiral Mullen were doing before Congress.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The Democrat who leads the House defense appropriations subcommittee, Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/john_p_murtha/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; p.=&quot;P.&quot; murtha.=&quot;Murtha.&quot;&gt;
  John P. Murtha
 &lt;/a&gt;
 of Pennsylvania, said Wednesday that he expected the White House to seek $40 billion by the spring to pay for the additional troops, or $10 billion more a year than the president estimated in his speech. Administration officials said they did not support efforts of some Democrats in Congress to pay for the additional troops with a surtax on incomes, meaning that war costs would continue to add to the deficit.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In a full day of testimony before the Senate Armed Services Committee and the House Foreign Affairs Committee, Mr. Gates, Mrs. Clinton and Admiral Mullen faced repeated criticism that the target date to begin withdrawals  less than a year after all the 30,000 troops arrive  would be an invitation to
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot;&gt;
  Taliban
 &lt;/a&gt;
 to prepare and plan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/john_mccain/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; john=&quot;John&quot; mccain.=&quot;McCain.&quot;&gt;
  John McCain
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Republican of Arizona, started the day by grilling Mr. Gates and Admiral Mullen, and said it made no sense to set an exit date if the withdrawal was also going to be based on conditions on the ground, as the president said in his speech.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Eight hours later on the House side, Mr. Gates was still answering the same question when he said: I have adamantly opposed deadlines. I opposed them in Iraq, and I oppose deadlines in Afghanistan. In Afghanistan, he said, This will be a gradual process.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The American commander in Afghanistan, Gen.
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/stanley_a_mcchrystal/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stanley=&quot;Stanley&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; mcchrystal.=&quot;McChrystal.&quot;&gt;
  Stanley A. McChrystal
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , made the same point while speaking to reporters in Kabul, the Afghan capital. He said he was absolutely supportive of the timeline laid out by Mr. Obama, but he also cautioned that the timeline was flexible and is not an absolute.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Its not, At 18 months, everybody leaves, the general said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The July 2011 date, Mr. Gates, Mrs. Clinton and Admiral Mullen said, was in large part meant to be a wake-up call to the Afghans that the United States would not be in the country forever. How do you demonstrate resolve and at the same time convey a sense of urgency to the Afghans that they must step up to the plate and begin to take responsibility for their own security and to protect their own country against the extremists? Mr. Gates told the House committee.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Although members of both parties expressed doubts about the war plan, there were few political fireworks. Representative
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/r/dana_rohrabacher/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; dana=&quot;Dana&quot; rohrabacher.=&quot;Rohrabacher.&quot;&gt;
  Dana Rohrabacher
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , a California Republican who opposes the war, dismissed Mr. Obamas strategy as maybe a different facade, but its the same old policy.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Over all, the hearings had little of the drama that characterized Capitol Hill hearings on the war in Iraq. In the morning, Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/evan_bayh/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; evan=&quot;Evan&quot; bayh.=&quot;Bayh.&quot;&gt;
  Evan Bayh
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Democrat of Indiana, offered his congratulations to Mrs. Clinton on the engagement of her daughter, Chelsea.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The hearings did offer a glimpse of a few details and some of the thinking behind the presidents strategy. The testimony from the three officials showed that the White House would keep to its longstanding goal to build up the Afghan security forces to 240,000 by 2011, and not expand to 400,000 as General McChrystal had proposed.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/l/carl_levin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; carl=&quot;Carl&quot; levin.=&quot;Levin.&quot;&gt;
  Carl Levin
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , the Michigan Democrat who has been a proponent of training more Afghan security forces, showed his own skepticism on that issue, and questioned whether sending so many additional troops might keep the Afghans from building up their security forces on their own. Where I have questions is whether the rapid deployment of a large number of U.S. combat forces, without an adequate number of Afghan security forces for our troops to partner with, serves that mission, he said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In his opening statement, Mr. Gates, who pushed for the 30,000 additional American troops and was singled out by the White House as influential in Mr. Obamas decision,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2009/09/04/us/politics/04military.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  sharply differed with some of Mr. Obamas advisers
 &lt;/a&gt;
 who have argued that the United States should focus on rooting out
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot;&gt;
  Al Qaeda
 &lt;/a&gt;
 from Pakistan, and that the Taliban in Afghanistan do not present a serious long-term threat to the national security of the United States.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 On the contrary, Mr. Gates said, Al Qaeda and the Taliban are inextricably linked.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 While Al Qaeda is under great pressure now and dependent on the Taliban and other extremist groups for sustainment, the success of the Taliban would vastly strengthen Al Qaedas message, to the Muslim world, that violent extremists are on the winning side of history, Mr. Gates said. He added, The Taliban and Al Qaeda have become symbiotic, each benefiting from the success and mythology of the other.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 When pressed by Senator
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/susan_collins/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; susan=&quot;Susan&quot; collins.=&quot;Collins.&quot;&gt;
  Susan Collins
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Republican of Maine, on why the United States had to invest so much military power and money in Afghanistan when Al Qaeda still had the ability to establish havens in other countries, Mr. Gates replied that Afghanistan was unique.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Not only was it the place where the 2001 attacks against the United States were planned, he said, it is still the wellspring of inspiration for extremist jihadism everywhere.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He said that the guidance and strategic leadership for Al Qaeda came from the groups leaders who were in the border area with Pakistan, and that there was an unholy alliance that had developed in the past year between Al Qaeda, the Taliban in Pakistan and the Taliban in Afghanistan.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He added, If anything, the situation, I think, is more serious today than it was a year ago because of the attacks of the Taliban in Pakistan on Pakistan, and the effort of Al Qaeda in collusion with the Taliban in Pakistan to try and destabilize Pakistan itself.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;authorId&quot;&gt;
  &lt;p&gt;
   Reporting was contributed by Jackie Calmes, Christopher Drew and Mark Landler from Washington, and Richard A. Oppel Jr. from Kabul, Afghanistan.
  &lt;/p&gt;

<node id="n12602">
<data key="x">1.63242375602</data>
<data key="y">0.7</data>
<data key="label">Kremlin Applause Is Faint as Obama Hails Arms Pact</data>
<data key="date">2010-03-27</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;/nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 MOSCOW  On a Friday that began in Washington with a
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.whitehouse.gov/blog/2010/03/26/president-obama-announces-new-start-treaty&quot; title=&quot;Video&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; text=&quot;text&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; conference=&quot;conference&quot; on=&quot;on&quot; whitehouse.gov=&quot;WhiteHouse.gov&quot;&gt;
  triumphant presidential news conference
 &lt;/a&gt;
 about the conclusion of arms talks with
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/russiaandtheformersovietunion/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; russia=&quot;Russia&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; post-soviet=&quot;Post-Soviet&quot; nations.=&quot;Nations.&quot; class=&quot;meta-loc&quot;&gt;
  Russia
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , Moscow seemed to have its mind on other things.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 President
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/dmitri_a_medvedev/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; dmitri=&quot;Dmitri&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; medvedev.=&quot;Medvedev.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
  Dmitri A. Medvedev
 &lt;/a&gt;
 was in Sochi, scolding Olympic trainers over their athletes dismal showing in Vancouver. Prime Minister
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/vladimir_v_putin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; vladimir=&quot;Vladimir&quot; v.=&quot;V.&quot; putin.=&quot;Putin.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
  Vladimir V. Putin
 &lt;/a&gt;
 gave a speech on the dangers posed by spring flooding. The highest-ranking Russian official to address reporters about the treaty was Foreign Minister Sergey V. Lavrov, who hastily gathered the press at dinnertime in a tiny ministry conference room.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mr. Lavrov called the agreement real progress in the relationship between Russia and the United States, but added that Russia could pull out if it concluded that the American missile defense plans had compromised its nuclear deterrent. Indeed, unease over missile defense was seeping into commentary even as officials hailed a mutual success.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Mikhail V. Margelov, the chairman of the foreign affairs committee in the upper house of Russias Parliament, said the document was neither a Russian gift to America nor an American gift to Russia. He acknowledged that the reception had been quiet, saying that was because negotiators were focused on finishing the job.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 We are on the edge of signing a treaty, so why make noise? Mr. Margelov said. I mean, speaking in colloquial language, let us drink Champagne when we accomplish the task.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In recent months Russian leaders  notably Mr. Putin  have pushed openly for a pact that explicitly links reductions in strategic weapons to limits on the American missile-defense program. Aleksei K. Pushkov, the host of the political talk show Post-Scriptum, said he feared that the text of the treaty included only a soft linkage between offense and defense. For many Russians, the first question will be, Where have we made concessions to the United States? he said, and they will look for the answer in those phrases.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 The treaty will be criticized by a number of people  people who are connected to the military, and political experts who will say it is a fig leaf which allows Russia to save face, but does not allow Russia to ask anything of the U.S., at least anything of substance, Mr. Pushkov said.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Should we have signed a treaty which does not give us any kind of serious guarantee? he said. This is something which will be debated.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 But if that conversation had begun on Friday, it was a quiet one. As Russias arsenal ages, the treaty will allow Moscow to maintain parity with the United States, which can afford a larger force, and arms talks serve to reassert its status as a nuclear superpower.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 Gen. Nikolai Y. Makarov, the chief of Russias general staff, spoke in favor of the pact, saying it will eliminate concerns on both sides and is fully in line with the security interests of Russia.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 One reason for Russian caution is the looming ratification vote in the
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/s/senate/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; u.s.=&quot;U.S.&quot; senate.=&quot;Senate.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
  United States Senate
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , where any note of Russian triumphalism might play badly. Russias opposition is too weak to block ratification here, though Mr. Margelov said he expected vigorous criticism from Communists in Parliament, for whom, as he put it, any agreement with the United States is considered a kind of betrayal of the motherland.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 He said he hoped they would all come to see the agreement for what it was: a compromise.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 All foreign policy is compromise, he said. I dont think we have to report to our public that it was a great diplomatic victory for Russia. And our American colleagues should not deceive their public by saying it was a great American victory. It was a compromise. There is nothing wrong with that word.
&lt;/p&gt;

<node id="n13508">
<data key="x">1.72712680578</data>
<data key="y">0.1</data>
<data key="label">News Analysis: Obama Sticks to a Deadline in Iraq </data>
<data key="date">2010-04-28</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;/nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  When
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 approved a plan to withdraw combat forces from
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; iraq.=&quot;Iraq.&quot; class=&quot;meta-loc&quot;&gt;
  Iraq
 &lt;/a&gt;
 this summer, it was based on the assumption that a newly elected government would be in place by the time Americans headed home. Fourteen months later, that assumption is exploding but the plan remains the same.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleInline&quot; runaroundleft=&quot;runaroundLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--h--&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;columnGroup&quot; doublerule=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;sectionHeader&quot;&gt;
   Related
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;ul class=&quot;headlinesOnly&quot; multiline=&quot;multiline&quot; flush=&quot;flush&quot;&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2010/04/28/world/middleeast/28baghdad.html?ref=middleeast&quot;&gt;
      Report Details Torture at Secret Baghdad Prison
     &lt;/a&gt;
     (April 28, 2010)
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     Times Topics:
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/index.html&quot;&gt;
      Iraq
     &lt;/a&gt;
     |
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html&quot;&gt;
      Barack Obama
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
  &lt;/ul&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;inlineImage&quot; module=&quot;module&quot;&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;icon&quot; enlargethis=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2010/04/28/world/28iraq_CA1/28iraq_CA1-articleInline.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;127&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;h6 class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
   Joao Silva for The New York Times
  &lt;/h6&gt;
  &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
   Gen. Ray Odierno, left, the commander in Iraq, says he is comfortable with the withdrawal plan.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleBody&quot;&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The delay and messy aftermath of the Iraqi election mean it may be months before the next government is formed, even as tens of thousands of American troops pack to leave. Yet Mr. Obama has not had a meeting on Iraq with his full  national security team in months, and the White House insists that it has no plans to revisit the withdrawal timetable.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The situation presents a test for Mr. Obamas vow to end the  war, perhaps the most defining promise he made when he ran for president. While Mr. Obama has proved flexible about other campaign promises and deadlines, his plan to pull out combat forces by August and the remaining 50,000 trainers and advisers by December 2011 has been the most inviolate of policies.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  By sticking to the deadline, Mr. Obama effectively is abandoning the thesis he adopted on the recommendation of military and civilian advisers in February 2009 that a large American military presence was needed long enough to provide stability during the post-election transition.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Instead, the president is now relying on the conclusion that Iraqis are stepping up to the challenges of governing and security that for too long depended on Americans.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  We see no indications now that our planning needs to be adjusted, said Ben Rhodes, a deputy national security adviser to Mr. Obama. We did anticipate an extended period of government formation, and recent Iraqi-led missions that have
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2010/04/20/world/middleeast/20baghdad.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
   killed leaders of Al Qaeda in Iraq
  &lt;/a&gt;
  show their growing capacity to provide for security, which of course is critical to ending our combat mission at the end of August.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  While Mr. Obama has not convened a full-scale meeting on Iraq lately, Mr. Rhodes noted that  Vice President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Joseph R. Biden Jr.
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , who manages Iraq policy, does hold such meetings regularly and keeps Mr. Obama informed.  Its something that hes obviously regularly engaged in, Mr. Rhodes said of the president.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  For Mr. Obama, shifting the deadline would prove complicated for both logistical and political reasons. As he pulls troops out of Iraq, he has been sending more to Afghanistan, putting pressure on the armed forces. And with his liberal base angry at the Afghan troop buildup, any delay of the Iraq drawdown could provoke more consternation on the left.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But the resistance to revisiting the deadline has drawn concern from former American officials, including some who participated in formulating the Obama policy last year. The original plan anticipated Iraqi elections in December and the formation of a new government at least 60 days afterward. Instead, the elections did not take place until March and produced a near tie between the parties of Prime Minister
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/nuri_kamal_al-maliki/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nuri=&quot;Nuri&quot; kamal=&quot;Kamal&quot; al-maliki.=&quot;al-Maliki.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Nuri Kamal al-Maliki
  &lt;/a&gt;
  and former Prime Minister
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/a/iyad_allawi/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; iyad=&quot;Iyad&quot; allawi.=&quot;Allawi.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Ayad Allawi
  &lt;/a&gt;
  . And now the two are fighting through the courts and recounts.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/c/ryan_c_crocker/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ryan=&quot;Ryan&quot; c.=&quot;C.&quot; crocker.=&quot;Crocker.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Ryan C. Crocker
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , the former American ambassador to Iraq who was appointed by President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   George W. Bush
  &lt;/a&gt;
  and later made recommendations to Mr. Obama regarding the drawdown, said the administration should  consider extending the August deadline.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  I am a little bit nervous, Mr. Crocker, now dean of the Bush School of Government and Public Service at
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/texas_a_and_m_university/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; texas=&quot;Texas&quot; a=&quot;A&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; m=&quot;M&quot; university=&quot;University&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Texas AThe elections were later than expected and there were very close results between Maliki and Allawi, which suggest its going to be a very long process. We may not even have a new government until were at the August deadline. Id like the U.S. to retain the original flexibility.
  &lt;/a&gt;
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Meghan L. OSullivan, a former deputy national security adviser to Mr. Bush who oversaw Iraq policy, also said August might be too soon.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Im for a shift away from the current rigid deadline to something more flexible, more reflective of the fluid and tense situation in Iraq, where the last thing the Iraqis really need is for the United States to be focused more on exit than anything else at a moment of high political uncertainty, she said.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Two former officials who worked on Iraq policy in the Obama administration said that after it became clear how late the elections would be, Gen.
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/ray_odierno/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ray=&quot;Ray&quot; odierno.=&quot;Odierno.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Ray Odierno
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , the commander in Iraq, wanted to keep  3,000 to 5,000 combat troops in northern Iraq after the Aug. 31 deadline. But the officials, who spoke on condition of anonymity because of the delicacy of the matter, said it was clear that the White House did not want any combat units to remain.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Brig. Gen. Stephen R. Lanza, a spokesman for General Odierno, said no formal request to the White House was ever made. Nor, he added, has the president ever denied him the tools needed to complete our mission.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  General Odierno, as well as his commander, Gen.
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   David H. Petraeus
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , and the  ambassador, Christopher J. Hill, have all said in recent days that they are satisfied with the current timetable.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  I feel very comfortable with our plan, General Odierno said on Fox News Sunday last week, and unless something unforeseen and disastrous happens, I fully expect us to be at 50,000 by the first of September.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  General Petraeus, in an interview, said the remaining force is still a substantial number that should be capable of handling the situation. The whole process of drawing down and getting to the change in the mission is on track, he said, and what were seeing in the wake of elections has included efforts by
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda_in_mesopotamia/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda=&quot;Qaeda&quot; in=&quot;in&quot; mesopotamia.=&quot;Mesopotamia.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Al Qaeda in Iraq
  &lt;/a&gt;
  once again to ignite sectarian violence, but we have not seen any success in that regard.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Some military analysts who have favored higher troop levels in Iraq in the past agreed that the current timetable still made sense. Michael E. OHanlon, a scholar at the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/b/brookings_institution/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; brookings=&quot;Brookings&quot; institution=&quot;Institution&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Brookings Institution
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , said staying longer would mean only that Americans could be enmeshed in deciding between Mr. Maliki and Mr. Allawi. I dont see why we should be picking sides in a top-down civil war, he said.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;nyt_author_id&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;authorIdentification&quot;&gt;
   &lt;p&gt;
   &lt;/p&gt;
   &lt;p&gt;
    Peter Baker reported from Washington, and Rod Nordland from Baghdad. Thom Shanker and Elisabeth Bumiller contributed reporting from Washington.
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_author_id&gt;

  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_correction_bottom&gt;
