<node id="n15040">
<data key="x">1.82182985554</data>
<data key="y">0.7</data>
<data key="label">Obama Hopes to Build Economic Relations With Russia</data>
<data key="date">2010-06-23</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;/nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 In his quest to restore relations with
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/russiaandtheformersovietunion/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; russia=&quot;Russia&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; post-soviet=&quot;Post-Soviet&quot; nations.=&quot;Nations.&quot; class=&quot;meta-loc&quot;&gt;
  Russia
 &lt;/a&gt;
 ,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 focused first on security issues like disarmament and Iran. But with
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2010/04/09/world/europe/09prexy.html&quot; title=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
  an arms control treaty signed
 &lt;/a&gt;
 and sanctions against Tehran approved, Mr. Obama hopes this week to open a new phase intended to build the robust economic relationship that has eluded his predecessors.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleInline&quot; runaroundleft=&quot;runaroundLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--forceinline--&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;columnGroup&quot; doublerule=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;h6 class=&quot;sectionHeader&quot;&gt;
   Multimedia
  &lt;/h6&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;columnGroup&quot; first=&quot;first&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
    &lt;div class=&quot;wideThumb&quot;&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
      &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2010/06/23/world/europe/23policy-graphic/23policy-graphic-thumbWide.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;126&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/div&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
      Trading With Russia
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h6&gt;
    &lt;h6 class=&quot;byline&quot;&gt;
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleBody&quot;&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  At Mr. Obamas invitation, President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/dmitri_a_medvedev/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; dmitri=&quot;Dmitri&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; medvedev.=&quot;Medvedev.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Dmitri A. Medvedev
  &lt;/a&gt;
  traveled to the United States on Tuesday, stopping first in California to woo Silicon Valley technology companies to help build his own Russian center of innovation. On Thursday, the two presidents will meet at the White House to discuss expanding trade and investment.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The focus on economic cooperation is intended to take the relationship between the two countries to a new level after years of mutual suspicion that peaked in 2008 during Russias war with Georgia, its small neighbor to the south. We want to develop a multidimensional relationship with Russia, said Michael McFaul, Mr. Obamas top Russia adviser. This trip will build on the foundation of these core security interests.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  If Mr. Obama can open up economic avenues, that could further the emerging partnership. I think of those mutually beneficial economic ties as ballast that could keep the overall relationship on an even keel even when adverse political winds threaten to blow us off course, said Edward S. Verona, president of
  &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.usrbc.org/&quot; title=&quot;The&quot; councils=&quot;councils&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
   the U.S.-Russia Business Council
  &lt;/a&gt;
  .
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Obama has already revived a civilian nuclear cooperation agreement that could be lucrative to Russia, and he will have what Mr. McFaul called a pretty serious discussion with Mr. Medvedev about how to secure Russian membership in the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/w/world_trade_organization/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; world=&quot;World&quot; trade=&quot;Trade&quot; organization.=&quot;Organization.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   World Trade Organization
  &lt;/a&gt;
  after 17 years of talks. Russia is by far the largest economy outside the 153-nation organization, which sets rules for international trade, and Mr. Medvedev expressed frustration that we have been led around by the nose for a long time, as he told The Wall Street Journal last week.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  An agreement between the two presidents on Russias W.T.O. accession could take away the remaining hurdles, said Anders Aslund, a Russia specialist at the Peterson Institute for International Economics in Washington. It would be a game changer for Russias domestic development, rendering the economy more open and competitive, while integrating Russia more firmly in the international community.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But expanding economic relations may prove harder than negotiating an arms treaty. Since the end of the cold war, every American president has talked about forging closer trade and investment ties with Russia, but with limited success. The United States did only $24 billion in trade with Russia last year  double the figure of just a few years ago, but still less than trade with Brazil, Taiwan or South Korea and a small fraction of the $366 billion in trade with China last year.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  One reason is the lack of a genuine rule of law in Russia. Foreign companies and investors have found themselves subject to capricious or even corrupt decisions by the Russian government and politically connected moguls with little real recourse in a judicial system that still defers to the Kremlin or local authorities.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Take the cases of three men as examples:
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/k/mikhail_b_khodorkovsky/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; mikhail=&quot;Mikhail&quot; b.=&quot;B.&quot; khodorkovsky.=&quot;Khodorkovsky.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Mikhail B. Khodorkovsky
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , once Russias richest man and its most successful capitalist, was in talks to sell a stake in his
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/o/oil_spills/gulf_of_mexico_2010/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; oil=&quot;oil&quot; spills.=&quot;spills.&quot; class=&quot;meta-classifier&quot;&gt;
   oil
  &lt;/a&gt;
  company to Exxon Mobil or ChevronTexaco when he was arrested in a political dispute with the Kremlin in 2003. He has been behind bars ever since and is on trial again in Moscow on what independent analysts consider trumped-up charges.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  William F. Browder, once the largest foreign portfolio investor in Moscow, was denied entry to the country in 2005 and had his companies used in what he says was a huge fraud scheme. A lawyer he had hired, Sergei Magnitsky, was arrested and died in prison last year when the authorities withheld medical treatment.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Robert Dudley was chief executive of BPs joint venture with Russian oil moguls, called
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/business/companies/tnk_bp/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; tnk-bp.=&quot;TNK-BP.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   TNK-BP
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , until a fight over control of the company led to problems renewing his visa and ultimately forced him out of the country in 2008. He is now managing BPs response to the Gulf of Mexico oil spill.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Browder is now waging a campaign warning American businesses away from Russia, briefing corporate lawyers for companies that Mr. Medvedev will visit and the staffs of several California lawmakers.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Medvedev is on a trip to attract U.S. technology companies to come to Russia and saying many nice things about the rule of law and modernization, when, in fact, the difference between his words and reality could not be more stark, Mr. Browder said. My advice to U.S. technology companies is to steer clear of Russia because its insanity to go there. They not only will risk their money, but also the lives of their employees.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Others argue that American investment only props up the current authoritarian system.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Western capital helps to support the status quo, said Lilia Shevtsova, an analyst at
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.carnegie.ru/?lang=en&quot; title=&quot;The&quot; centers=&quot;centers&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
   the Carnegie Moscow Center
  &lt;/a&gt;
  . It injects financial and technological
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/health/diseasesconditionsandhealthtopics/viagra_drug/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;Recent&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; archival=&quot;archival&quot; health=&quot;health&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; viagra.=&quot;Viagra.&quot; class=&quot;meta-classifier&quot;&gt;
   Viagra
  &lt;/a&gt;
  to the existing system. Western capital could become an engine of modernization only under new rules of the game  that is, when Russia moves toward real competition and rule of law.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Toby Gati, a strategic adviser to companies working in Russia, was more optimistic. We have the beginnings of a new mind-set on both sides, with the Russians now developing a stake in working with the U.S. for mainly economic reasons, said Ms. Gati, who works for the law firm Akin Gump.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But to make it work, she said, Moscow needs to guarantee property rights and rule of law: These are things Medvedev has spoken about, to his credit, she said, but so far he has done little to make them happen.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Medvedev is arguing that Russia is open for business. He met with American business leaders in St. Petersburg last week and agreed to have dinner in San Francisco on Tuesday night with Silicon Valley pioneers invited by former Secretary of State
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/s/george_p_shultz/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; p.=&quot;P.&quot; shultz.=&quot;Shultz.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   George P. Shultz
  &lt;/a&gt;
  . On Wednesday, he will visit Silicon Valley to draw investment and inspiration for a Russian version in the Moscow suburb of Skolkovo.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Among the supporters of his initiative is
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/s/eric_e_schmidt/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; eric=&quot;Eric&quot; e.=&quot;E.&quot; schmidt.=&quot;Schmidt.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Eric E. Schmidt
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , chief executive of Google, who said he thought greater technology cooperation would force changes in Russias business environment.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  My personal view, Mr. Schmidt said in an e-mail message, is that the presence of such technical companies, especially with foreign partnerships, are a great way to get the openness, transparency and societal change needed for the Russians to continue their development into a modern first-world government. Their presence in Russia will help pressure the incumbents who fear change and will also clearly benefit the citizens over all.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;nyt_correction_bottom&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;articleCorrection&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_correction_bottom&gt;
 &lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n15251">
<data key="x">1.9165329053</data>
<data key="y">0.7</data>
<data key="label">Despite Arrests, Obama Works to Rebuild Ties With Russia</data>
<data key="date">2010-07-01</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;/nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  They doffed their jackets and bonded over burgers, talking about everything from trade and geopolitics to their families. Everything, that is, except the spies that the government of one had hidden in a house just a few miles away and that the government of the other was about to arrest.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleInline&quot; runaroundleft=&quot;runaroundLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--forceinline--&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;columnGroup&quot; doublerule=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;sectionHeader&quot;&gt;
   Related
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;ul class=&quot;headlinesOnly&quot; multiline=&quot;multiline&quot; flush=&quot;flush&quot;&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2010/07/01/world/europe/01spy.html?ref=europe&quot;&gt;
      Released on Bail in Cyprus, Spy Ring Suspect Vanishes
     &lt;/a&gt;
     (July 1, 2010)
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2010/07/01/nyregion/01children.html?ref=europe&quot;&gt;
      Accused of Espionage, but Praised as Moms and Dads
     &lt;/a&gt;
     (July 1, 2010)
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2010/07/01/nyregion/01towns.html?ref=europe&quot;&gt;
      Our Towns: When the Roads to Suburbia Lead to a Suspected Spy Ring
     &lt;/a&gt;
     (July 1, 2010)
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     Times Topics:
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/r/russian_spy_ring_2010/index.html&quot;&gt;
      Russian Spy Ring (2010)
     &lt;/a&gt;
     |
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/e/espionage/index.html&quot;&gt;
      Espionage
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
  &lt;/ul&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleBody&quot;&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The roundup of a suspected Russian spy ring did more than disrupt a years-old deep-cover operation inside the United States  it cast a shadow over
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   President Obama
  &lt;/a&gt;
  s effort to transform the relationship between the two countries. The timing of the arrests, coming barely 72 hours after President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/m/dmitri_a_medvedev/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; dmitri=&quot;Dmitri&quot; a.=&quot;A.&quot; medvedev.=&quot;Medvedev.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Dmitri A. Medvedev
  &lt;/a&gt;
  s White House visit, frustrated Mr. Obamas team. But as prosecutors assemble their case, Mr. Obama has resolved not to let the ghosts of the 20th century get in the way of his goals in the 21st.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Obamas administration said Wednesday that it would not expel Russian diplomats and it expressed no indignation that its putative partner was spying on it. Mr. Obamas plan is to largely ignore the issue publicly, leaving it to diplomats and investigators to handle, while he moves on to what he sees as more important matters.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  We would like to get to the point where there is just so much trust and cooperation between the United States and
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/russiaandtheformersovietunion/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; russia=&quot;Russia&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; post-soviet=&quot;Post-Soviet&quot; nations.=&quot;Nations.&quot; class=&quot;meta-loc&quot;&gt;
   Russia
  &lt;/a&gt;
  that nobody would think of turning to intelligence means to find out things that they couldnt find out in other channels, Philip Gordon, the assistant secretary of state in charge of Russia, told reporters. Were apparently not there yet. I dont think anyone in this room is shocked to have discovered that.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But the spy scandal could embolden critics who argue that Mr. Obama has been overly optimistic about his capacity to reset a relationship freighted by longstanding suspicion and clashing interests. The episode could complicate Mr. Obamas efforts to persuade the Senate to approve the new arms control treaty he negotiated with Mr. Medvedev.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  It ought to reset our rosy view of Russia and remind us that Russia is not a trustworthy ally, Senator
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/christopher_s_bond/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; christopher=&quot;Christopher&quot; s.=&quot;S.&quot; bond.=&quot;Bond.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Christopher S. Bond
  &lt;/a&gt;
  of Missouri, the ranking Republican on the Senate intelligence committee, said in an interview. Harking back to
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/r/ronald_wilson_reagan/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; ronald=&quot;Ronald&quot; wilson=&quot;Wilson&quot; reagan.=&quot;Reagan.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Ronald Reagan
  &lt;/a&gt;
  s approach, Mr. Bond said: We have to deal with them. But wasnt there a great president who said, Trust but verify?
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Even if Mr. Obama can assuage doubts on the treaty, the scandal has underscored the limits of the new relationship.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The spy scandal is unlikely to derail the reset because both sides have too much invested in the success of the current agenda, said Angela E. Stent, a former National Intelligence Council official now at
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/g/georgetown_university/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; georgetown=&quot;Georgetown&quot; university=&quot;University&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Georgetown University
  &lt;/a&gt;
  . But it is a cautionary reminder that the U.S.-Russian relationship remains a selective partnership where cold war legacies persist.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Part of the problem for Mr. Obama is that his desire to redefine the relationship has been misinterpreted as an effort to redefine Russia itself, said
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.americanprogress.org/experts/CharapSam.html&quot; title=&quot;His&quot; official=&quot;official&quot; biography=&quot;biography&quot;&gt;
   Samuel Charap
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , a scholar at the Center for American Progress, a liberal research organization close to the White House. Its a reminder that yes, Russia is still Russia and Putin is still Putin, he said of the spy case, referring to Prime Minister
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/vladimir_v_putin/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; vladimir=&quot;Vladimir&quot; v.=&quot;V.&quot; putin.=&quot;Putin.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Vladimir V. Putin
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , a former K.G.B. colonel. None of that is Obamas fault. The intention was never to reset Russia.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  It should come as little surprise, of course, that the two countries still spy on each other two decades after the end of the cold war. Even close allies like Israel have been caught spying here. Recent history shows that Washington and Moscow have been able to get past such moments when they were determined to pursue other agendas.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   George W. Bush
  &lt;/a&gt;
  faced such a challenge at the start of his presidency with the arrest of
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/h/robert_philip_hanssen/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; philip=&quot;Philip&quot; hanssen.=&quot;Hanssen.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Robert Hanssen
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , a longtime
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/f/federal_bureau_of_investigation/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; federal=&quot;Federal&quot; bureau=&quot;Bureau&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; investigation.=&quot;Investigation.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   F.B.I.
  &lt;/a&gt;
  agent caught working for Russia. Mr. Bush kicked out 50 Russian diplomats and Moscow did the same to 50 American diplomats. But three months later, he met Mr. Putin, then president, and declared that he had seen the soul of a partner he could work with.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  This case should be easier to overcome without tit-for-tat expulsions because the suspected spy ring did not seem to achieve any serious breach of national security. As
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.aei.org/scholar/2&quot; title=&quot;His&quot; official=&quot;official&quot; biography=&quot;biography&quot;&gt;
   Leon Aron
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , a Russian expert at the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/american_enterprise_institute_for_public_policy_research/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; american=&quot;American&quot; enterprise=&quot;Enterprise&quot; institute=&quot;Institute&quot; for=&quot;for&quot; public=&quot;Public&quot; policy=&quot;Policy&quot; research.=&quot;Research.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   American Enterprise Institute
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , the conservative research organization, noted: The relationship survived Aldrich Ames and Robert Hanssen. That was serious stuff and everybody rolled with the punches.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Russian leaders appear interested in playing down the situation. Although Moscow initially called the charges baseless, the Foreign Ministry later took that statement off its Web site and confirmed that the suspects were Russian citizens. Mr. Putin said the American authorities had gotten out of control in making the arrests, but then minimized it by saying relations will not suffer. Much of the Russian commentary suggested that the arrests were an effort by dark forces in the American government to undermine Mr. Obamas reset policy.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  In a telephone call between Sergei Prikhodko, Mr. Medvedevs foreign policy adviser, and Gen.
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/j/james_l_jones/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; james=&quot;James&quot; l.=&quot;L.&quot; jones.=&quot;Jones.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   James L. Jones
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , Mr. Obamas national security adviser, the Russian emphasized that Moscow wanted to resolve the issue without jeopardizing positive changes in the relationship, people briefed on the call said.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The timing of this was obviously a bit awkward, coming just after Mr. Medvedevs visit, said Andrew C. Kuchins, a Russia scholar at the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/c/center_for_strategic_and_international_studies/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; center=&quot;Center&quot; for=&quot;for&quot; strategic=&quot;Strategic&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; international=&quot;International&quot; studies.=&quot;Studies.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Center for Strategic and International Studies
  &lt;/a&gt;
  . But, he said, we have a fair amount of history of delinking spy scandals from the rest of Russia policy.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Suspect Disappears in Cyprus
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  ATHENS  The 11th suspect in the  Russian spy ring case   has disappeared on the Mediterranean island of Cyprus, where he was arrested but released on bail Tuesday.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Late Wednesday, a police spokesman told the Cyprus state news agency that the suspect, Christopher Metsos, 54, had failed to report as required to a precinct in the islands southwest, where he had been apprehended. The police obtained a warrant for his arrest and a manhunt was under way.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Metsos, who is accused of being the spy rings paymaster, was arrested early Tuesday at the airport in the southern city of Larnaca as he was about to fly to Budapest.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  In a move that dismayed American law enforcement authorities, a local court ordered his release on bail of around $25,000 on the condition that he surrender his passport while arrangements were made for his extradition to the United States.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  &lt;strong&gt;
   NIKI KITSANTONIS
  &lt;/strong&gt;
 &lt;/p&gt;

<data key="x">2.01123595506</data>
<data key="y">0.4</data>
<data key="label">In Speech on Iraq, Obama Reaffirms Drawdown</data>
<data key="date">2010-08-02</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;/nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 ATLANTA  Nearly eight years after he denounced what he called a dumb war in Iraq and nearly two years after he won the White House promising to end it,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 marked the formal conclusion  of the combat mission in a country still finding its way in a new era.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleInline&quot; runaroundleft=&quot;runaroundLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--forceinline--&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;inlineImage&quot; module=&quot;module&quot;&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2010/08/03/us/03prexy-polfront/03prexy-polfront-articleInline-v2.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;146&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; /&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;h6 class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
   Doug Mills/The New York Times
  &lt;/h6&gt;
  &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
   President Obamas appearance before the Disabled American Veterans group was the first of several similar events in coming weeks to draw attention to the transition in Iraq.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;columnGroup&quot; doublerule=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;sectionHeader&quot;&gt;
   Related
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;ul class=&quot;headlinesOnly&quot; multiline=&quot;multiline&quot; flush=&quot;flush&quot;&gt;
   &lt;li&gt;
    &lt;h6&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2010/08/03/us/politics/03prexy-text.html?ref=politics&quot;&gt;
      Text: Obamas Remarks on the Iraq Drawdown
     &lt;/a&gt;
     (August 3, 2010)
    &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;/li&gt;
  &lt;/ul&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;columnGroup&quot; doublerule=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;thumbnail&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/roomfordebate/2010/08/02/getting-the-troops-out-of-iraq?ref=politics&quot;&gt;
     &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com//images/2010/08/02/opinion/rfd75.jpg&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; alt=&quot;border=0&quot; /&gt;
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;h3&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/roomfordebate/2010/08/02/getting-the-troops-out-of-iraq?ref=politics&quot;&gt;
     Getting the Troops Out of Iraq
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h3&gt;
   &lt;h6 class=&quot;byline&quot;&gt;
   &lt;/h6&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
    What are the risks of Obamas timetable for withdrawing from Iraq?
   &lt;/p&gt;
   &lt;ul class=&quot;refer&quot;&gt;
    &lt;li&gt;
     &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/section/opinion/comment_icon.gif&quot; alt=&quot;Comment&quot; width=&quot;9&quot; height=&quot;11&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; /&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/roomfordebate/2010/8/2/getting-the-troops-out-of-iraq&quot;&gt;
      Post a Comment
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/li&gt;
   &lt;/ul&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;sectionHeader&quot;&gt;
   Blog
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;runaroundRight&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/thecaucus/thecaucus75.gif&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; alt=&quot;/&quot; /&gt;
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;h3&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     The Caucus
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h3&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
    The latest on President Obama, his administration and other news from Washington and around the nation.
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     Join the discussion.
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/p&gt;
   &lt;ul class=&quot;refer&quot;&gt;
    &lt;li&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/pages/politics/index.html&quot;&gt;
      More Politics News
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/li&gt;
   &lt;/ul&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleBody&quot;&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  As a candidate for president, I pledged to bring the war in Iraq to a responsible end, Mr. Obama told a convention of Disabled American Veterans in Atlanta on Monday. Shortly after taking office, I announced our new strategy for Iraq and for a transition to full Iraqi responsibility. And I made it clear that by August 31, 2010, Americas combat mission in Iraq would end. And that is exactly what we are doing  as promised and on schedule.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  By the end of this month,  the American force in Iraq will have shrunk to just 50,000 troops, from 144,000. The remaining advise and assist brigades will officially focus on supporting and training Iraqi security forces, protecting American personnel and facilities and mounting counterterrorism operations. Those 50,000 troops are due to leave by the end of 2011.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Obamas  appearance before the veterans group is the first of  several similar events in coming weeks meant to draw attention to the transition in Iraq. While he has gone months without mentioning the war much in public as he focused on tightening regulation of the financial industry and stopping the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/o/oil_spills/gulf_of_mexico_2010/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; oil=&quot;oil&quot; spills.=&quot;spills.&quot; class=&quot;meta-classifier&quot;&gt;
   oil spill
  &lt;/a&gt;
  in the Gulf of Mexico, the president is now trying to remind Americans of one of his most important decisions.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The high-level public focus on Iraq appears aimed at least in part at blunting some of the growing frustration, particularly among his liberal base, over the war in Afghanistan. The president essentially is arguing to skeptics in the public and in Congress that he is bringing at least one war to a conclusion and can do so with another eventually as well.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  A fact sheet prepared by the White House, for instance, pointedly notes that even with his troop buildup in Afghanistan, the drawdown in Iraq means that the total number of uniformed Americans in the two countries will have dropped from 177,000 when he took office to about 146,000 by the end of August.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But with the Afghan conflict now the longest-running war in American history and casualties rising in July to their highest level since it began nearly nine years ago, Mr. Obama may have difficulty offsetting the growing anxiety about one war by claiming success in another. In the House, 102 Democrats voted last week against a $59 billion spending bill to pay for the two wars, 70 more than the number who voted against a similar measure last year.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The replacement of the commanding general in Afghanistan and the publication by
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/w/wikileaks/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; wikileaks.=&quot;WikiLeaks.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   WikiLeaks
  &lt;/a&gt;
  of tens of thousands of secret United States military reports have focused attention on the struggles in turning around the war. The number of troops in Afghanistan has tripled since Mr. Obama took office,  but he has ordered that some of them begin pulling out by July 2011.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The tension over that deadline was evident on a talk show on Sunday, when the House speaker,
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/nancy_pelosi/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; nancy=&quot;Nancy&quot; pelosi.=&quot;Pelosi.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Nancy Pelosi
  &lt;/a&gt;
  ,  and Defense Secretary
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Robert M. Gates
  &lt;/a&gt;
  outlined starkly different ideas of what they hope or anticipate will happen next summer. Just last month, Vice President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Joseph R. Biden Jr.
  &lt;/a&gt;
  played down the July 2011 start of a withdrawal, saying it could mean pulling out as few as a couple thousand troops.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Ms. Pelosi made clear she found that unsatisfactory. I hope it is more than that, she said on This Week on ABC. I know its not going to be turn out the lights and lets all go home on one day. But I do think the American people expect it to be somewhere between that and a few thousand troops.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But Mr. Gates, appearing on the same program, said he hopes to limit any troop pullout at first. My personal opinion is that drawdowns early on will be of fairly limited numbers, he said.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Obama made no reference on Monday to the withdrawal deadline before the veterans group, where it might not be as popular as it is with his supporters, but instead vowed to continue pursuing radicals in Afghanistan, noting that
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda.=&quot;Qaeda.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Al Qaeda
  &lt;/a&gt;
  plotted the attacks of Sept. 11, 2001, from there.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  If Afghanistan were to be engulfed by an even wider insurgency, Al Qaeda and its terrorist affiliates would have even more space to plan their next attack, he said. And as president of the United States, I refuse to let that happen.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But Mr. Obama argued that his strategy in Afghanistan was beginning to show results.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Its important that the American people know that we are making progress and we are focused on goals that are clear and achievable, he said.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  With Iraq, Mr. Obama has stuck to his withdrawal schedule despite changing conditions on the ground. He promised during the campaign to pull out combat forces within 16 months. But after taking office he extended that to 19 months to give the Iraqis enough time to hold a new election, assemble a fresh government and get through a transition with the security of a robust American force.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;div id=&quot;pageLinks&quot;&gt;

 &lt;/div&gt;

  &lt;div class=&quot;articleCorrection&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_correction_bottom&gt;
 &lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n16565">
<data key="x">2.10593900482</data>
<data key="y">0.4</data>
<data key="label">News Analysis: In Iraq, Obama Faces Balancing Act as Combat Mission Ends</data>
<data key="date">2010-08-21</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;/nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  The official end of Americas combat mission in Iraq next week will fulfill the campaign promise that helped vault
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 to the White House, but it also presents profound risks as he seeks to claim credit without issuing a premature declaration of victory.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleInline&quot; runaroundleft=&quot;runaroundLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--forceinline--&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;h3 class=&quot;sectionHeader&quot;&gt;
   Blog
  &lt;/h3&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;runaroundRight&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/thecaucus/thecaucus75.gif&quot; height=&quot;75&quot; width=&quot;75&quot; alt=&quot;/&quot; /&gt;
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;h3&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     The Caucus
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h3&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
    The latest on President Obama, his administration and other news from Washington and around the nation.
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://thecaucus.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     Join the discussion.
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/p&gt;
   &lt;ul class=&quot;refer&quot;&gt;
    &lt;li&gt;
     &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/pages/politics/index.html&quot;&gt;
      More Politics News
     &lt;/a&gt;
    &lt;/li&gt;
   &lt;/ul&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleBody&quot;&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  As columns of vehicles crossed the border and troops arrived to happy homecomings last week, Mr. Obama released a restrained written statement and made a one-sentence reference at a pair of fund-raisers. While some called it the end of the seven-year war, Mr. Obama sought to avoid the sort of
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2003/11/03/us/white-house-letter-a-proclamation-of-victory-that-no-author-will-claim.html?&quot; title=&quot;New&quot; york=&quot;York&quot; times=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
   mission accomplished moment
  &lt;/a&gt;
  that haunted his predecessor.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But the White House wants to find a way to mark the moment and remind voters just two months before midterm elections that he delivered on his vow to pull out combat forces. Mr. Obama plans to make a high-profile speech on the drawdown next week, and aides are discussing whether to have him meet with returning troops. Vice President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/joseph_r_jr_biden/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; joseph=&quot;Joseph&quot; r.=&quot;R.&quot; biden=&quot;Biden&quot; jr.=&quot;Jr.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Joseph R. Biden Jr.
  &lt;/a&gt;
  will address the Veterans of Foreign Wars in Indianapolis on Monday.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The symbolism of the departing troops that played out on network television masked the more complex reality on the ground. Even as the last designated combat forces leave and the mission formally changes on Aug. 31 to a support role, 50,000 American advise and assist troops will remain in the country for 16 months more, still in harms way and still armed for combat if necessary. Whats more, Iraqs future remains fraught with challenges amid a stubborn political impasse and a continuing low-grade insurgency.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Political posturing is the norm in Washington, and claiming victory and an end to a war is far more popular than bearing the burden of leadership and dealing with reality,
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://csis.org/expert/anthony-h-cordesman&quot; title=&quot;Bio&quot; on=&quot;on&quot; centers=&quot;centers&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
   Anthony H. Cordesman
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , a military specialist at the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/c/center_for_strategic_and_international_studies/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; center=&quot;Center&quot; for=&quot;for&quot; strategic=&quot;Strategic&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; international=&quot;International&quot; studies.=&quot;Studies.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Center for Strategic and International Studies
  &lt;/a&gt;
  in Washington,
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://csis.org/publication/iraq-mission-accomplished-mark-ii&quot; title=&quot;Article&quot; on=&quot;on&quot; centers=&quot;centers&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
   wrote on the centers Web site
  &lt;/a&gt;
  on Friday. The Iraq war is not over and it is not won. In fact, it is at as critical a stage as at any time since 2003.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Denis R. McDonough, chief of staff of the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/n/national_security_council/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; national=&quot;National&quot; security=&quot;Security&quot; council=&quot;Council&quot;&gt;
   National Security Council
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , said the administration had no illusions.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Does anybody believe the violence is going to stop entirely and the opponents to stability and progress in Iraq are going to stand down? No, he said. But we do know that the Iraqi security forces are in a position to take that role on themselves increasingly.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The official transition from Operation Iraqi Freedom to Operation New Dawn is as much a change in labels as it is a change in mission. With violence far below its peak in 2006 and 2007, American forces have increasingly taken a back seat to the Iraqi security units they trained.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But after seven years of a war started by President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   George W. Bush
  &lt;/a&gt;
  on the basis of false intelligence, the desire for finality, and perhaps closure, has focused attention on this moment and provoked a fresh discussion in Washington about what it all has meant.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  After hundreds of billions of dollars, more than 4,400 American military deaths and at least 100,000 Iraqi civilian deaths and perhaps many more, was it worth it? Did toppling a dictator and nursing a fledgling if flawed democracy make a difference? And did the United States salvage credibility by sticking it out and finally stabilizing Iraq even if not winning the clear-cut victory originally envisioned?
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  If we cant have a victory parade, we at least ought to be able to make some definitive conclusions, said
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.bu.edu/ir/faculty/alphabetical/bacevich/&quot; title=&quot;Bio&quot; on=&quot;on&quot; university=&quot;university&quot; web=&quot;Web&quot; site=&quot;site&quot;&gt;
   Andrew J. Bacevich
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , a military specialist at
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/b/boston_university/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; boston=&quot;Boston&quot; university=&quot;University&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Boston University
  &lt;/a&gt;
  who lost a son in Iraq and has written a new book,
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.newsweek.com/blogs/we-read-it/2010/08/02/washington-rules-america-s-path-to-permanent-war.html&quot; title=&quot;Newsweek&quot; review=&quot;review&quot;&gt;
   Washington Rules: Americas Path to Permanent War.
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.newsweek.com/blogs/we-read-it/2010/08/02/washington-rules-america-s-path-to-permanent-war.html&quot; title=&quot;Newsweek&quot; review=&quot;review&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/a&gt;
  And it just doesnt seem that we are going to do so. We want to just move on, sadly.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  In part, that owes to the deteriorating situation in Afghanistan, where Mr. Obama is sending more troops, as well as the fragile economy at home, where millions of Americans are looking for work. And so while his opposition to the Iraq war animated his early candidacy, it seems almost a secondary issue these days.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  During a fund-raising speech in Ohio last week, for instance, Mr. Obama mentioned the Iraq transition only in passing. We are keeping the promise I made when I began my campaign for the presidency: by the end of this month, we will have removed 100,000 troops from Iraq, and our combat mission will be over in Iraq, he said, a line he later repeated at a fund-raiser in Miami.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  As they mark the moment, Democrats generally make no mention of the troop buildup and strategy change ordered by Mr. Bush in 2007, which many credit with turning around the war and making it possible to end combat now. By the time Mr. Bush left office, he had sealed an agreement with Iraq to withdraw all American troops by the end of 2011. After taking office, Mr. Obama added an intermediary deadline of drawing down to 50,000 by the end of this month.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Bush showed up unannounced at the Dallas-Fort Worth International Airport earlier this month to greet troops returning from Iraq. While no news media were invited,
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nNt4J8l5ft4We&quot; can=&quot;can&quot; take=&quot;take&quot; a=&quot;a&quot; certain=&quot;certain&quot; measure=&quot;measure&quot; of=&quot;of&quot; satisfaction=&quot;satisfaction&quot; from=&quot;from&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; success=&quot;success&quot; in=&quot;in&quot; iraq=&quot;Iraq&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/l_paul_iii_bremer/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; l.=&quot;L.&quot; paul=&quot;Paul&quot; bremer=&quot;Bremer&quot; iii.=&quot;III.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   L. Paul Bremer III
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , the former Iraqi occupation administrator, said in an interview. Its not a complete success yet, obviously, but building democracy takes time.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  He added that a successful Arab-Muslim democracy basically puts the lie to the Islamic extremists who maintain that democracy is anathema to Islam and advocate a harsh form of rule.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/h/stephen_j_hadley/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; stephen=&quot;Stephen&quot; j.=&quot;J.&quot; hadley.=&quot;Hadley.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Stephen J. Hadley
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , who was Mr. Bushs national security adviser, said the current transition was due to the surge ordered by the former president and opposed by Mr. Obama when he was a senator. But he said he was glad that Mr. Obamas team has gone through a transition and that it seemed to be taking pride in accomplishments in Iraq. He said he hoped that the administration would see the task through.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  If they do, they can rightly claim some measure of credit, and I would be the first to give them credit, Mr. Hadley said. But they need to stay focused and stay engaged.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  For Mr. Obama, this moment is a reminder of the lesson his predecessor learned after
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2003/05/02/world/aftereffects-the-president-bush-declares-one-victory-in-a-war-on-terror.html?&quot; title=&quot;New&quot; york=&quot;York&quot; times=&quot;Times&quot; article=&quot;article&quot;&gt;
   declaring the end of major combat
  &lt;/a&gt;
  operations on an aircraft carrier in front of a Mission Accomplished banner in 2003. Iraq was a messy war with no tidy end. There will be no surrender ceremony on the deck of a battleship, Mr. Bush later concluded.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Obama has come to the same realization, in almost the exact same words.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  There will be no simple moment of surrender to mark the journeys end, he declared last spring.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;nyt_correction_bottom&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;articleCorrection&quot;&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_correction_bottom&gt;
 &lt;nyt_update_bottom&gt;
 &lt;/nyt_update_bottom&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;</data><data key="labelPos">n</data></node>
<node id="n16809">
<data key="x">2.20064205457</data>
<data key="y">0.1</data>
<data key="label">Obama Tells Troops, Our Task in Iraq Is Not Yet Over</data>
<data key="date">2010-08-31</data>
<data key="dummy">0</data>
<data key="text">&lt;nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;/nyt_correction_top&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
 WASHINGTON  The United States may be bringing troops home from the war in
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/news/international/countriesandterritories/iraq/index.html?inline=nyt-geo&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; news=&quot;news&quot; and=&quot;and&quot; information=&quot;information&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; iraq.=&quot;Iraq.&quot; class=&quot;meta-loc&quot;&gt;
  Iraq
 &lt;/a&gt;
 , but there is a tough slog ahead in the war in Afghanistan,
 &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/o/barack_obama/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; barack=&quot;Barack&quot; obama.=&quot;Obama.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
  President Obama
 &lt;/a&gt;
 told troops in Fort Bliss, Texas on Tuesday.
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleInline&quot; runaroundleft=&quot;runaroundLeft&quot;&gt;
 &lt;!--forceinline--&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;columnGroup&quot; doublerule=&quot;doubleRule&quot;&gt;
  &lt;!--at war promo --&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;story&quot;&gt;
   &lt;h5&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/blogs_v3/atwar/atwar190.gif&quot; alt=&quot;At&quot; war=&quot;War&quot; /&gt;
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/h5&gt;
   &lt;p class=&quot;summary&quot;&gt;
    Notes from Afghanistan, Pakistan, Iraq and other areas of conflict in the post-9/11 era.
    &lt;a href=&quot;http://atwar.blogs.nytimes.com&quot;&gt;
     Go to the Blog
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/p&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div class=&quot;inlineImage&quot; module=&quot;module&quot;&gt;
  &lt;div class=&quot;image&quot;&gt;
   &lt;div class=&quot;icon&quot; enlargethis=&quot;enlargeThis&quot;&gt;
    &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
     Enlarge This Image
    &lt;/a&gt;
   &lt;/div&gt;
   &lt;a href=&quot;javascript:pop_me_up2(&quot;&gt;
    &lt;img src=&quot;http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2010/09/01/world/01militaryspan-cnd/01militaryspan-cnd-articleInline.jpg&quot; width=&quot;190&quot; height=&quot;149&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; /&gt;
   &lt;/a&gt;
  &lt;/div&gt;
  &lt;h6 class=&quot;credit&quot;&gt;
   Morry Gash/Associated Press
  &lt;/h6&gt;
  &lt;p class=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;
   Defense Secretary Robert M. Gates spoke on Tuesday at the American Legion convention in Milwaukee.
  &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;readerscomment&quot; class=&quot;inlineLeft&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;articleBody&quot;&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Speaking just hours before he is to deliver an Oval Office address commemorating what is supposed to be the end of combat in Iraq, where some 50,000 troops will remain until next year in a mainly advisory and training role, Mr. Obama nonetheless warned that the American mission is not yet accomplished. Mr. Obama told the troops that his Oval Office address is not going to be a victory lap; its not going to be self-congratulatory. Theres still a lot of work.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Obamas address tonight is meant to convey that he has kept one of the central promises of his campaign: withdrawing American combat troops from Iraq. But he is tiptoeing a fine line between taking credit for the withdrawal and echoing the mission accomplished tone that President Bush struck so famously seven years ago, and that came back to haunt Mr. Bush in the ensuing years as Iraq fell into further chaos.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Mr. Obama called Mr. Bush Tuesday morning from
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/subjects/p/presidents_and_presidency_us/air_force_one/index.html?inline=nyt-classifier&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; air=&quot;Air&quot; force=&quot;Force&quot; one.=&quot;One.&quot; class=&quot;meta-classifier&quot;&gt;
   Air Force One
  &lt;/a&gt;
  as he was enroute to Fort Bliss, White House officials said. The two spoke just for a few moments, Benjamin Rhodes, deputy national security adviser for strategic communications, told reporters aboard the plane, declining to give any additional detail about the conversation.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  In rolling out the promises-kept theme on the Iraq withdrawal, Mr. Obama is trying to reconcile his record of opposition to the war, and to the troop surge ordered by President Bush which many military officials credit for stemming violence in Iraq, with his role as a war-time commander seeking to credit his troops with a mission accomplished.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  While there were big debates about war and peace across the country, the president said, the one thing we dont argue about is that we have the finest fighting force in the history of the world. He got shouts of approval from the assembled Fort Bliss troops for that line. (The event was covered by a small pool of print and television reporters.)
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  The main message I have tonight and the main message I have to you is congratulations on a job well done, Mr. Obama said. The most pride I take in my job is being your commander in chief.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  On Afghanistan, Mr. Obama said that he is convinced that under the command of General
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/p/david_h_petraeus/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; david=&quot;David&quot; h.=&quot;H.&quot; petraeus.=&quot;Petraeus.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   David Petraeus
  &lt;/a&gt;
  , the latest American military commander in Afghanistan, we have the troops who are there in a position to start taking the fight to the terrorists. But he warned that there would be heavy casualties.Earlier in the day, Defense Secretary
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/g/robert_m_gates/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; robert=&quot;Robert&quot; m.=&quot;M.&quot; gates.=&quot;Gates.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   Robert M. Gates
  &lt;/a&gt;
  warned against premature victory parades or self-congratulations as American combat operations in Iraq drew officially to a close, and at the same time said that the success of United States forces in Afghanistan was only possible, not inevitable
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  In remarks to the American Legion in Milwaukee, Mr. Gates sounded a restrained, sober note about the state of Americas two wars.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  In Iraq, he said, the most recent elections have yet to result in a coalition government,
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/a/al_qaeda_in_mesopotamia/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; al=&quot;Al&quot; qaeda=&quot;Qaeda&quot; in=&quot;in&quot; mesopotamia.=&quot;Mesopotamia.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Al Qaeda in Mesopotamia
  &lt;/a&gt;
  is beaten but not gone, and sectarian tensions remain. He said the 50,000 United States troops still in Iraq would continue to work with Iraqi security forces, who only last week faced a flurry of coordinated insurgent attacks across the country that killed at least 51 people.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  I am not saying that all is, or necessarily will be, well in Iraq, Mr. Gates, who is one of Mr. Obamas most influential advisers, told the legion.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  In Afghanistan, he said, the
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/organizations/t/taliban/index.html?inline=nyt-org&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; the=&quot;the&quot; taliban.=&quot;Taliban.&quot; class=&quot;meta-org&quot;&gt;
   Taliban
  &lt;/a&gt;
  are a cruel and ruthless adversary, and are not going quietly. Their leadership, he said, has ordered a campaign of intimidation against Afghan civilians and is singling out women for brutal attacks.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  I know there is a good deal of concern and impatience about the pace of progress since the new strategy was announced last December, Mr. Gates said, referring to Mr. Obamas decision to send to Afghanistan 30,000 additional United States troops, who have finished arriving only this month. Total American forces in Afghanistan now number nearly 100,000.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  But in an attempt to draw a parallel between the current fragile stability of Iraq and what might be possible in Afghanistan, Mr. Gates said that the intensifying combat and rising casualties in Afghanistan were in many ways reminiscent of the early months of the surge of United States forces ordered in Iraq by President
  &lt;a href=&quot;http://topics.nytimes.com/top/reference/timestopics/people/b/george_w_bush/index.html?inline=nyt-per&quot; title=&quot;More&quot; articles=&quot;articles&quot; about=&quot;about&quot; george=&quot;George&quot; w.=&quot;W.&quot; bush.=&quot;Bush.&quot; class=&quot;meta-per&quot;&gt;
   George W. Bush
  &lt;/a&gt;
  in 2007, when American troops were taking the highest losses of the war.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  Three and a half years ago very few believed the surge could take us to where we are today in Iraq, and there were plenty of reasons for doubts, said Mr. Gates, who helped make the surge decision as Mr. Bushs defense secretary at the time. But back then, this countrys civilian and military leadership chose the path we believed had the best chance of achieving our national security objectives, as we are doing in Afghanistan today.
 &lt;/p&gt;
 &lt;p&gt;
  He added: Success there is not inevitable. But with the right strategy and the willingness to see it through, it is possible. And it is certainly worth the fight.
 &lt;/p&gt;
